ANIMALS
§ 90.01 DEFINITIONS.
   (A)   Terms or words used herein shall be interpreted as follows.
      (1)   The present tense includes the past or future tense. The singular
includes the plural and the plural includes the singular.
      (2)   The word SHALL is mandatory; the word MAY is permissive; and the
word SHOULD is preferred.
      (3)   The masculine shall include the feminine.
   (B)   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
      ANIMAL SHELTER. Any premises designated by the city for the purpose of
impounding and caring for animals held under authority of this subchapter.
      AT LARGE. Off the premises of the custodian and not under control of the
custodian or a member of his or her immediate family, or an agent or employee
of the custodian, by cord or chain sufficiently strong to prevent the animal
from escaping.
      CRUEL or CRUELTY. Any or all of the following:
         (a)   The intentional and malicious infliction of pain, physical
suffering, injury, or death upon an animal;
         (b)   To maliciously kill, maim, wound, overdrive, overload, drive
when overloaded, overwork, torture, torment, deprive of necessary sustenance,
drink, or shelter, cruelly beat, mutilate, or cruelly kill an animal;
         (c)   To subject an animal to needless suffering, inflict unnecessary
cruelty, drive, ride, or otherwise use an animal when the same is unfit;
         (d)   To abandon an animal; or
         (e)   To negligently confine an animal in unsanitary conditions, or to
negligently house an animal in inadequate facilities; to negligently fail to
provide sustenance, water, or shelter to an animal.
      CUSTODIAN. Any person, firm, corporation, organization, or department
owning, possessing, or harboring or having the care or custody of any
livestock, fowl, and rabbits.
      LIVESTOCK. Includes all animals that are considered to be domesticated
animals, excluding in-house pets.
      POUND. A place enclosed by public authority for the detention of stray
animals.
      TETHERED. To fasten or restrain an animal by any means to an object so
that it can range only within a set radius.
(Prior Code, § 6-3-1) (Ord. 2000-08, passed 10-9-2000)
§ 90.02 APPLICABILITY OF SUBCHAPTER.
   This subchapter shall not apply to the keeping and maintaining of dogs,
cats, exotic animals, and other in-house pets. This subchapter is intended to
regulate the keeping and maintaining of all livestock, fowl, and rabbits.
(Prior Code, § 6-3-2) (Ord. 2000-08, passed 10-9-2000)
§ 90.03 REGULATIONS FOR MAINTAINING CERTAIN ANIMALS AND FOWL.
   (A)   Fowl. It shall be unlawful to keep or maintain any fowl, rabbits, or
livestock, which includes, but is not limited to, horses, cows, sheep, goats,
or other domesticated animals, within the city limits, except as provided in
this subchapter. For the purposes of this division (A), FOWL shall mean
domesticated birds (galliformes and anseriformes), and shall include chickens,
ducks, and geese but shall not include peafowl, guinea fowl, ostriches, or
emus.
   (B)   Required area for fowl.
      (1)   To maintain and keep fowl, there must be at least 5,000 square feet
of open space of real property for each six fowl which are more than 12 weeks
from hatch and one additional fowl more than 12 weeks from hatch for each
additional 1,250 square feet of open space of real property and/or up to 25
fowl not more than 12 weeks from hatch, and in no event shall any person keep
or maintain more than 12 fowl more than 12 weeks from hatch, and in no event
shall the coop and/or run be less than 60 feet from a dwelling other than that
of the owner or person keeping or maintaining the fowl.
      (2)   It shall be unlawful for a person to keep or maintain male fowl
within the city limits except for a time period not to exceed 12 weeks from
hatch, as demonstrated by the person keeping or maintaining such male fowl.
   (C)   Required area for rabbits. To maintain and keep rabbits, there must be
at least 5,000 square feet of open space of real property for each 25 rabbits,
and in no event shall any person keep or maintain more than 50 rabbits, and in
no event shall the rabbit hutch or rabbit run be less than 60 feet from a
dwelling other than that of the owner.
   (D)   Required area for livestock. To maintain or keep one cow, one horse,
one goat, one sheep, one llama, or one of any other domesticated animal, the
custodian must have at least one acre (43,560 square feet) of pasture of real
property available for one animal and one-half acre (21,780 square feet) for
each additional animal. The space occupied by any building and any area
excluded from access by the animals, except buildings to be occupied by the
animals, for which the calculation is being made, shall be excluded. The
required area for any animal or the animals shall be considered only one time.
For example, the one acre considered for one horse may not be considered as the
required area for one cow or one of any other domesticated animal.
   (E)   Property configuration. The property which may be considered in making
up the square footage must be ADJOINING or ADJACENT, which shall be deemed to
mean not separated by a distance greater than the width of a street. It shall
not be necessary that the animals have continual access to all of the property,
but all property being considered in making up the square footage shall be
devoted primarily to the use of the animals.
   (F)   Property ownership. The property making up the required area must be
owned or leased by the animal custodian or the custodian must have written
authorization from the property owner to use the property for the purpose of
grazing or maintaining animals
   (G)   Fences. Fences enclosing such animals must be so constructed as to
prevent the animals from going upon the property of adjoining property owners
in any manner whatsoever and must comply with fencing specifications of this
code.
   (H)   Enclosures and structures. Animal pens, corrals, or any other premises
or structure used for the keeping of or maintaining any animal or fowl, shall
be kept in a clean, sanitary, and humane condition. Said enclosure or structure
shall be kept in such a manner as to keep said animals or fowl confined at all
times.
   (I)   Nuisance control. All animals must be controlled and maintained by
their custodian so that they do not threaten the safety and/or disturb the
comfort and repose of any reasonable person.
(Prior Code, § 6-3-3) (Ord. 2000-08, passed 10-9-2000; Ord. 2021-001, passed 1-
27-2021) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.04 ABUSE, NEGLECT, AND CRUELTY.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to treat any animal in a harmful or
injurious way or to disregard or be remiss in the care or treatment of any
animal. Any person found abusing or neglecting any animal shall pay a fine
established by resolution adopted by the City Council from time to time. Any
person found guilty of cruelty shall be prosecuted under Idaho Code § 25-3520A.
(Prior Code, § 6-3-4) (Ord. 2000-08, passed 10-9-2000) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.05 GRAZING IN STREETS AND ALLEYS PROHIBITED.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to stake, by rope or otherwise, for the
purpose of feeding or grazing any animal on, in or about any street or alley
within the corporate limits of the city. If any animal be staked, roped or
fastened in any manner, in or upon any street or alley for the purpose above
mentioned, said animal shall be deemed at large and shall be impounded as
herein provided.
(Prior Code, § 6-3-5) (Ord. 2000-08, passed 10-9-2000) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.06 PERMISSION REQUIRED TO MOVE ANIMALS.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to drive or cause to be driven any loose
animals or fowl whatsoever in, on, through, or across any street or alley
within the corporate limits of the city without first having obtained the
consent of either the Mayor, Chief of Police, or City Council. Any person may
drive one head of any such loose animal or fowl through or across any street or
alley without first having obtained such consent. In the event animals or fowl
shall have escaped from their enclosure, it shall not be necessary to obtain
permission to return the animals to an enclosure.
(Prior Code, § 6-3-6) (Ord. 2000-08, passed 10-9-2000) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.07 ANIMALS PROHIBITED ON SIDEWALK.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to permit or allow any animal or fowl,
while the same is being ridden or led, to travel upon any of the sidewalks
situated within the corporate limits of the city.
(Prior Code, § 6-3-7) (Ord. 2000-08, passed 10-9-2000) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.08 ANIMALS AND FOWL AT LARGE PROHIBITED.
   Animals and fowl shall not be allowed to run at large or to be herded in any
of the streets, alleys, parks, or public places or upon private property,
except those being driven through for shipment or being moved from one property
to another. The custodian shall obtain permission from owner of said private
property.
(Prior Code, § 6-3-8) (Ord. 2000-08, passed 10-9-2000) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.09 ANIMALS AND FOWL TO BE TAKEN UP.
   Any animal or fowl found running at large within the corporate limits of the
city may be taken up by any officer or by any person and delivered to the Chief
of Police or person deemed his or her agent and placed in a pound. Such
impounded animal or fowl shall be provided with proper care, food, and water
while so confined. The custodian shall be responsible for all boarding fees.
(Prior Code, § 6-3-9) (Ord. 2000-08, passed 10-9-2000)
§ 90.10 NOTICE OF IMPOUNDMENT.
   The Chief of Police or City Clerk shall give immediate notice to the
custodian, if known, of the impoundment of such animal or fowl. If no action is
taken within 48 hours after notice, the Chief of Police or City Clerk shall
post two notices of sale, containing a description of the animal or fowl and
the time and place of sale. Such notice shall be posted in two public places
within the city, one of which shall be the front door of the City Hall.
(Prior Code, § 6-3-10) (Ord. 2000-08, passed 10-9-2000)
§ 90.11 SALE OF IMPOUNDED ANIMALS OR FOWL.
   If any animal or fowl so impounded is unclaimed by its custodian after six
days from the date of posting of said notice, the Chief of Police or his or her
agent shall sell the same at public auction. The proceeds of such sale, after
deducting legal fees and all expenses, shall be paid into the City Treasury.
(Prior Code, § 6-3-11) (Ord. 2000-08, passed 10-9-2000)
§ 90.12 RECLAIMING ANIMALS OR FOWL BEFORE SALE.
   If at any time before such sale, the custodian of any impounded animal or
fowl shall claim the same, he or she shall be entitled to the possession
thereof only after payment of all legal charges and expenses incident to such
impounding.
(Prior Code, § 6-3-12) (Ord. 2000-08, passed 10-9-2000)
§ 90.13 IMPOUNDING FEES.
   The city shall be entitled to receive as administrative fees for taking up
and impounding any livestock, fowl, or rabbits, a sum set by resolution and
passed by the City Council from time to time.
(Prior Code, § 6-3-13) (Ord. 2000-08, passed 10-9-2000)
§ 90.14 CUSTODIAN MAY RECEIVE PROCEEDS OF SALE.
   If the custodian of any personal property sold under the provisions of this
subchapter shall, at any time within 14 days from the date of such sale, make
satisfactory proof to the Chief of Police or his or her agent of his or her
ownership, he or she shall be entitled to receive the net proceeds of such sale
on deposit in the City Treasury. The failure of the custodian to make such
proof within such period shall result in a waiver by the custodian of any claim
to said net proceeds which the custodian would otherwise have.
(Prior Code, § 6-3-14) (Ord. 2000-08, passed 10-9-2000)
§ 90.15 LOADING PENS AND SALE YARDS.
   It shall be unlawful to keep livestock, fowl, or rabbits in loading pens or
sale yards within the corporate limits of the city, except by written
permission of the City Council.
(Prior Code, § 6-3-15) (Ord. 2000-08, passed 10-9-2000) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.16 PIGS.
   It shall be unlawful to maintain a pig within the corporate limits of the
city, except as specifically provided in §
90.18.
(Prior Code, § 6-3-16) (Ord. 2000-08, passed 10-9-2000) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.17 WILD OR UNDOMESTICATED ANIMALS.
   It shall be unlawful to keep or maintain any animal which is of a species
considered to be wild or undomesticated, including, but not limited to, the
following: cougar/mountain lion, bear, skunk, raccoon, bobcat, eagle, hawks,
alligators, python (six feet and larger), rattlesnakes, copperhead snake,
porcupine, elk, deer, wolverines, crocodile, panther, camel, ostrich, rhea,
emu, owls, weasels (excluding ferrets), mink, badger, lynx, all foxes, coyote,
wolf, water moccasin snake, coral snake, African lion, Bengal tiger,
coatimundi, primate, buffalo, or zebra, unless such animal is part of a bona
fide circus or animal show licensed to perform in the state, or is otherwise
licensed as provided in this subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 6-3-17) (Ord. 2000-08, passed 10-9-2000) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.18 PERMITS.
   Custodians of a pig or of a wild or undomesticated animal may apply for a
permit to keep such animal within the corporate limits of the city. A fee set
by resolution and passed by the City Council shall be paid with each
application. The permit may be revoked without refund if any custodian is found
to be in violation of any section of this subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 6-3-18) (Ord. 2000-08, passed 10-9-2000)
§ 90.19 TIME ALLOWED FOR COMPLIANCE.
   This subchapter shall apply to all animals and fowl now within the corporate
limits of the city and to those subsequently brought into the city. Any person
now keeping animals or fowl shall comply with all requirements of this
subchapter within 60 days from its effective date.
(Prior Code, § 6-3-19) (Ord. 2000-08, passed 10-9-2000)
§ 90.20 NUISANCE BY ANIMALS.
   (A)   The following acts are hereby declared to be public nuisances and
shall be considered an infraction, punishable by a fine as set by resolution
and passed by the City Council from time to time:
      (1)   Maintaining or keeping any animal or fowl in violation of any of
the requirements of this subchapter;
      (2)   Allowing dead fowl or animal bodies (or portions thereof) to remain
upon the ground or in stables or in the particular animal run longer than six
hours;
      (3)   Burning any manure, or animal or fowl droppings and feathers within
the city limits;
      (4)   Allowing obnoxious odors to emanate from barns, manure piles, or
animal enclosures;
      (5)   Keeping unsightly, smelly, dilapidated animal enclosures; and
      (6)   Leaving solid excrement on public areas or on private property. If
droppings are cleaned up immediately, the infraction shall not apply.
   (B)   Nothing contained in this subchapter shall be interpreted to constrain
the right of any person to proceed with a civil action for damages and/or to
abate any nuisance.
(Prior Code, § 6-3-20) (Ord. 2000-08, passed 10-9-2000) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.21 OTHER ACTS PROHIBITED.
   The following acts are prohibited and shall be considered an infraction,
punishable by a fine as set by resolution and passed by the City Council from
time to time.
   (A)   No person shall wilfully open any door or gate on any private premises
or untether or coax away an animal for the purpose of enticing or enabling any
animal to leave such private premises and be at large, as defined in this
subchapter.
   (B)   No person shall wilfully provoke, mistreat, or abuse any animal while
confined to its custodian’s premises.
   (C)   No person shall set a leg hold type of trapping device to catch an
animal.
   (D)   No person shall abandon any animal by dropping off or leaving such
animal on any public street, alley, sidewalk, or in any city park or playground
or other public place or building, or on the premises of another.
(Prior Code, § 6-3-21) (Ord. 2000-08, passed 10-9-2000) Penalty, see §
90.99
DOGS
§ 90.35 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions apply unless
the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   ANIMAL SHELTER. Any premises designated by the city for the purpose of
impounding and caring for animals held under authority of this subchapter.
   AT LARGE. Off the premises of the owner and not under control of the owner
or a member of his or her immediate family, or an agent or employee of the
owner, by leash, cord, or chain sufficiently strong to prevent the dog from
escaping.
   DOG. Both male and female of the family canis familiaris.
   LEASH. A cord, chain, or rope of the length to restrict the dog to the
owner’s property and, when the dog is off the owner’s property, the LEASH shall
be not more than eight feet in length.
   OWNER. Any person, firm, corporation, organization, or department possessing
or harboring or having the care or custody of a dog.
   TETHERED. To fasten or restrain a dog by any means to an object so that it
can range only within a set radius.
   UNCONFINED. Pertains to a vicious dog and shall mean not securely confined
indoors or confined in a securely enclosed and locked pen or structure upon the
premises of the owner of the dog. The pen or structure must have secure sides
and a secure top attached to the sides. If the pen or structure has no bottom
secured to the sides, the sides must be embedded into the ground no less than
one foot. All such pens or structures must be adequately lighted and kept in a
clean and sanitary condition.
   VICIOUS DOG. Any dog with a known propensity, tendency, or disposition to
attack unprovoked, to cause injury to, or otherwise threaten the safety of
human beings or domestic animals; or any dog which, because of its size,
physical nature, or vicious propensity, is capable of inflicting serious
physical harm or death to humans or which would constitute a danger to human
life or property if it were not kept in the manner required by this subchapter;
or any dog which, without provocation, attacks or bites, or has attacked or
bitten, a human being or domestic animal; or any dog owned or harbored
primarily or in part for the purpose of dogfighting, or any dog trained for
dogfighting.
(Prior Code, § 6-2-1) (Ord. 2000-05, passed 7-24-2000)
§ 90.36 REGISTRATION REQUIRED; FEES.
   All dogs kept, harbored, or maintained by their owners in the municipality
shall be registered with the city by the age of six months. Only after
compliance with the provisions of §
90.48 (proof of vaccination) shall dog identification tags be issued by the
City Clerk and/or designated agents upon payment of a registration fee for each
dog. The owner shall state at the time application is made for such
registration and upon printed forms provided for such purpose, his or her name
and address and description of the dog to be registered in such manner that the
dog may be identified with reasonable certainty, and the name to which the dog
answers. Each registration issued under the provisions of this subchapter shall
be valid for the lifetime of the animal. Animal identification tags may also be
issued for animals in the fringe areas outside the city. Fees for dog
registrations and other fees shall be set by the City Council from time to
time, by resolution.
(Prior Code, § 6-2-2) (Ord. 2000-05, passed 7-24-2000) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.37 EXCEPTIONS.
   The licensing provisions of §
90.36 shall not apply to dogs whose owners are nonresidents within the
municipality for less than 30 days. Seeing eye dogs properly trained to assist
blind persons, when such dogs are actually being used by blind persons for the
purpose of aiding them in going from place to place, shall be licensed without
charge. New owners and new residents may purchase licenses at the regular fees
if the license is purchased within 30 days of acquisition of dog or
establishing residence. It shall be the owner’s responsibility to show proof of
the date of ownership or establishment of residence.
(Prior Code, § 6-2-3) (Ord. 2000-05, passed 7-24-2000)
§ 90.38 TAG AND COLLAR.
   Upon payment of the registration fee, the Clerk and/or designated agent
shall issue to the owner a registration certificate and a metallic tag for each
dog so registered. The number shall correspond with the number on the
certificate. Each owner shall provide each dog with a collar to which the
identification tag must be affixed and shall see that the collar and tag are
constantly worn by the dog. In case a dog tag is lost or destroyed, a duplicate
tag will be issued by the Clerk upon presentation of receipt showing the
payment of the registration fee and the payment of a fee to be set by the City
Council, from time to time, by resolution, for each duplicate. Dog tags shall
not be transferable from one dog to another and no refunds shall be made on any
dog identification fee because of death of the dog or the owner leaving the
municipality.
(Prior Code, § 6-2-4) (Ord. 2000-05, passed 7-24-2000)
§ 90.39 RUNNING AT LARGE.
   No owner or keeper of any dog shall allow or let such dog to run at large
within the corporate limits of the municipality at any time of the year. No
owner or keeper of any dog shall leave such dog tethered on public property or
in such a manner as to be on public property for longer than 30 minutes while
owner is conducting business.
(Prior Code, § 6-2-5) (Ord. 2000-05, passed 7-24-2000) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.40 NUISANCE BY DOGS.
   (A)   It is hereby declared to be unlawful for any owner, keeper,
controller, or harborer of any animal to allow or let his or her animal to
discharge such animal’s solid excrement upon public property or private
property, other than the property of the owner, keeper, controller or harborer.
However if such owner, keeper, controller, or harborer does immediately
thereafter remove and clean up such animal’s solid excrement from the property,
the nuisance shall be deemed remedied.
   (B)   It shall be unlawful for any person to cause, permit, or allow any dog
or dogs owned, harbored, controlled, or kept by him or her in the municipality
to remain outside of the dwelling of such person while such animal is causing
excessive or frequent howling, yelping, barking, whining, or the making of any
other noise which disturbs or is likely to disturb the comfort and repose of
any reasonable person; provided, that no person shall be prosecuted under this
division (B) unless written notice of the noise has been issued by a police
officer to the property owner or person in possession of the property wherein
the animal is located, or the animal’s owner, keeper, controller, or harborer,
or is left at the premises where the animal is located, at least 24 hours but
not more than 30 days prior to the filing of a formal complaint.
   (C)   Any person convicted of a violation of this section shall be punished
by fine to be set by the City Council, from time to time, by resolution.
Nothing contained in this subchapter shall be interpreted to constrain the
right of any person to proceed with a civil action for damages and/or to abate
any noise nuisance.
(Prior Code, § 6-2-6) (Ord. 2000-05, passed 7-24-2000) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.41 IMPOUND FACILITIES.
   The Chief of Police is hereby authorized and empowered to secure and
maintain a suitable impound facility approved by the City Council for the
purpose of carrying out the provisions of this subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 6-2-7) (Ord. 2000-05, passed 7-24-2000)
§ 90.42 IMPOUNDING.
   (A)   It is the duty of every police officer or other designated official to
apprehend any dog found running at large, untethered, or unlicensed contrary to
the provisions of this subchapter, or any dog which has attacked or bitten any
person or other animal and to impound such dog in an animal shelter or other
suitable place; provided, that if any fierce, dangerous, or vicious dog found
running at large cannot be safely taken up and impounded, such dog may be slain
by any police officer or other designated official.
   (B)   Any police officer or other designated official, upon receiving any
dog, shall make a complete registry, entering the breed, color, and sex of such
dog and whether wearing a license tag. If licensed, the police officer or other
designated official shall enter the name and address of the owner and the
number of the license tag. Licensed dogs shall be separated from unlicensed
dogs. If the owner is known or may be determined, the police officer or other
designated official may issue to the owner or persons responsible a notice of
offense or violation and fine. Such notice shall not be issued for any offense
or violation, unless the offense or violation is committed in the presence of
the police officer or other designated official, or a citizen has signed a
complaint against the dog and/or owner.
(Prior Code, § 6-2-8) (Ord. 2000-05, passed 7-24-2000)
§ 90.43 NOTICE TO OWNERS.
   Not later than one day after the impoundment of any dog, the owner shall be
notified, or if the owner of the dog is unknown, written notice shall be posted
for three days at three or more conspicuous places, one of which shall be the
City Hall, describing the dog and the time of taking. The owner of any dog so
impounded may reclaim such dog upon payment of the license fee, if unpaid,
penalties, and all cost and charges incurred for impounding, keeping, and
maintenance of said dog, and for adoption or euthanasia. Said charges shall
include a minimum fee for the first day of impoundment and an additional charge
over the boarding fee for each following consecutive day of impoundment. The
impounding charge shall be doubled each time that said dog is impounded, but no
impounding charge for any dog shall be in excess of four times the initial
impound fee. All fees and charges shall be established by resolution adopted by
the City Council from time to time.
(Prior Code, § 6-2-9) (Ord. 2000-05, passed 7-24-2000)
§ 90.44 DISPOSITION OF UNCLAIMED, VICIOUS, OR INFECTED DOGS.
   It is the duty of any police officer, or other designated official, to keep
all dogs so impounded for a period of 24 hours. If at the expiration of six
days from the date of notice to the owner of the date of posting of such
notice, such dog shall not have been redeemed, it may be destroyed or sold for
a sum of money sufficient to discharge the cost and charges incurred by the
municipality for impounding and keeping the dog, together with the license fee
(if applicable) for the current year if unpaid. Any police officer or other
designated official has authority to submit terminally ill, injured, or unfit
dog, after a reasonable search has been made for the owner, to a licensed
veterinarian to determine whether the dog can recover. If not, he or she may
authorize euthanasia of the dog; provided, that no dog which appears to be
suffering from rabies nor any dog of fierce, dangerous, or vicious propensities
shall be released from the pound but shall be destroyed. The buyer of any dog
under the provisions of this section shall become the owner of the dog free
from any claimer title of the original owner or harborer.
(Prior Code, § 6-2-10) (Ord. 2000-05, passed 7-24-2000)
§ 90.45 CONFINEMENT AND SIGNS FOR VICIOUS DOGS.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for the owner of a vicious dog to permit the dog
to go unconfined.
   (B)   The owner of a vicious dog shall display, in a prominent place on his
or her premises, a clearly visible warning sign indicating that there is a
vicious dog on the premises. A similar sign is required to be posted on the pen
or kennel of the animal.
(Prior Code, § 6-2-11) (Ord. 2000-05, passed 7-24-2000) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.46 LEASH AND MUZZLE.
   The owner of a vicious dog shall not suffer or permit the dog to go beyond
the premises of the owner unless the dog is securely muzzled and restrained by
a chain or leash not to exceed a length of four feet, and under the physical
restraint of a person. The muzzle shall be made in a manner that will not cause
injury to the dog or interfere with the vision or respiration, but shall
prevent it from biting any human or animal.
(Prior Code, § 6-2-12) (Ord. 2000-05, passed 7-24-2000) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.47 RABIES; NOTICE.
   (A)   It is unlawful for any person knowing or suspecting a dog to have
rabies to allow such dog to be taken off his or her premises or beyond the
limits of the municipality without the written permission of the Chief of
Police or other designated official. Every owner, or other person, upon
ascertaining a dog is rabid, shall immediately notify the Chief of Police, or
other designated official, who shall remove the dog to an animal shelter or a
veterinary hospital.
   (B)   Any dog that bites a person or animal shall be quarantined for 15
days. If a police officer or other designated official determines that the risk
of the biting animal being infected with rabies is possible but not probable,
the quarantine may be on the premises of the keeper. A dog quarantined on the
premises of the keeper shall be securely confined in an enclosure which is at
least fenced on all sides and from which the dog cannot escape, and which is
not accessible to the public.
   (C)   If a police officer or other designated official determines that it is
probable that the biting dog is infected with rabies the police officer or
other designated official may require the keeper to surrender the dog for the
quarantine period to an animal shelter or place the dog in a veterinary
hospital. The keeper shall pay all cost incurred during a period of quarantine.
   (D)   Any dog for which probable cause exists to cause a police officer or
other designated official to believe that it may be rabid may be quarantined by
such police officer or other designated official under the terms and conditions
for biting dogs set forth in division (C) above.
   (E)   No person shall kill or cause to be killed any dog which has bitten a
person or other animal, or any dog suspected of being rabid, except as needed
to prevent immediate injury or death to another animal or to a person until
after the animal has been placed in quarantine and a diagnosis of suspected
rabies is made by a licensed veterinarian.
(Prior Code, § 6-2-13) (Ord. 2000-05, passed 7-24-2000) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.48 VACCINATION.
   It shall be required that each owner or keeper of each and every dog within
the corporate limits of the city shall present a certificate of rabies
vaccination immunization signed by a practicing veterinarian in order to obtain
a city dog license. Said certificate must indicate the date of vaccination and
the length of time immunization is effective.
(Prior Code, § 6-2-14) (Ord. 2000-05, passed 7-24-2000) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.49 INSURANCE.
   Owners of vicious dogs must, within 15 days of the effective date hereof,
provide proof to the City Clerk of public liability insurance in the amount of
at least $100,000, insuring the owner for any personal injuries inflicted by
his or her vicious dog.
(Prior Code, § 6-2-15) (Ord. 2000-05, passed 7-24-2000) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.50 OTHER ACTS PROHIBITED.
   (A)   No person shall willfully open any door or gate on any private
premises or unleash or coax any dog for the purpose of enticing or enabling any
dog to leave such private premises and be at large, as defined in this
subchapter.
   (B)   No person shall willfully provoke, mistreat, or abuse any dog while
confined to its keeper’s premises.
   (C)   No person shall set a leg hold type trapping device to catch a dog.
   (D)   No person shall abandon any dog by dropping off or leaving such animal
on any public street, alley, sidewalk, or in any city park or playground, or
other public place or building, or on the premises of another.
(Prior Code, § 6-2-16) (Ord. 2000-05, passed 7-24-2000) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code of ordinances.
   (B)   Any person who violates any provision of §§
90.35 through
90.50 shall be deemed guilty of an infraction and may be fined in an amount set
by the City Council, from time to time, by resolution.
(Prior Code, § 6-2-17) (Ord. 2000-05, passed 7-24-2000)
CHAPTER 91: NUISANCES
Section
   
91.01   Rubbish in alleys
   
91.02   Abandoned containers
   
91.03   Refuse in buildings; stagnant water
   
91.04   Weeds
   
91.05   Plastic bags or coverings
   
91.06   Nuisances defined

§ 91.01 RUBBISH IN ALLEYS.
   If rubbish or other impediment is allowed to accumulate or remain in the
alley, the Council, or the Fire Chief, Chief of Police, or other officer
designated by the Council, may notify the property owner or tenant, or both, of
the property next on which such accumulation or obstruction remains, to remove
the same within one week, or less time if consonant with public safety, and if
the same is not so removed within the time allowed, then the city may remove
the same and tax the costs of such removal against the said property as taxes,
together with reasonable fees and interest thereon.
(Prior Code, § 3-4-1) (Ord. 94, passed 6-4-1929; Ord. 2016-02, passed 12-14-
2015) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 91.02 ABANDONED CONTAINERS.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to leave or permit to remain outside of
any dwelling, building, or other structure, or within any unoccupied or
abandoned building, structure, or dwelling under his or her control, in a place
accessible to children, any abandoned, unattended, or discarded icebox,
refrigerator, or other container which has a door of lid, snap lock, or other
locking device which may not be released from the inside, without first
removing said door or lid, snap lock, or other locking device.
(Prior Code, § 6-4-1) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 91.03 REFUSE IN BUILDINGS; STAGNANT WATER.
   (A)   Prohibited. No person shall permit or suffer to be in or accumulate in
or upon any yard, lot, place, or premises or upon any street or sidewalk
adjacent to or abutting upon any lot, block, place, or premises, or in any
building or shed owned or occupied by him or her within the corporate limits,
any stagnant water or impure water, refuse, vegetable decay, or decaying
substance, garbage, or filth of any kind, nor suffer such yard, lot, place,
building, or premises to be or to remain in such condition as to cause or
create a nuisance or offensive smell or to pollute or render unhealthful the
atmosphere or the premises or thereby to be, become, cause, or create a public
nuisance.
(Prior Code, § 4-4-1)
   (B)   Time limit. Any person shall clean up said premises and abate such
nuisance within 48 hours after having received notice of the condition from the
Mayor or Council.
(Prior Code, § 4-4-2)
Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 91.04 WEEDS.
   (A)   Defined. The word WEEDS shall include all vegetable growth that is
troublesome, useless, or noxious.
(Prior Code, § 7-4-1)
   (B)   Removal of weeds required. All occupants or owners are hereby required
to destroy all weeds upon their premises to the center of the street or alley.
(Prior Code, § 7-4-2)
   (C)   Failure to comply. Whenever the growth of weeds advances to a
condition prohibited by this section, the municipality or its designated
official shall notify such occupant or owner to remove same. In default of this
being done, the municipality shall remove the same and the cost thereof shall
become a lien upon the property. Said lien shall be collected as provided by
statute.
(Prior Code, § 7-4-3)
Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 91.05 PLASTIC BAGS OR COVERINGS.
   (A)   Definition. The words PLASTIC COVERINGS, PLASTIC BAG, and PLASTIC
PACKAGE, when used in this section, shall mean any covering, package, or bag
made of any material sufficiently thin and pliable to respond to static
electricity created by contact with the human body to the extent that it clings
to the human skin or body.
(Prior Code, § 6-7-1)
   (B)   Warning required. It shall be unlawful for any person to have in his
or her possession, or to deliver as a cover or wrapper, any plastic bag that is
of sufficient size to fit over a child’s head, or any bag which, when open, has
an opening larger than 25 square inches or a capacity of more than 125 cubic
inches, unless there is, at all times, clearly printed on such bag or covering,
or a paper attached to such bag or covering, words in letters at least one-
fourth inch high as follows:
 
WARNING: To avoid danger of suffocation keep this bag (or covering) away from
babies and children. Do not use in cribs, beds, carriages, or play pens. This
is not a toy.
 
(Prior Code, § 6-7-2)
   (C)   Certain bags a nuisance. Any plastic bag, covering, or package not
carrying or accompanied by the printed warning as provided in division (B)
above is hereby declared a nuisance.
(Prior Code, § 6-7-3)
Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 91.06 NUISANCES DEFINED.
   Anything which is injurious to the health or morals, or indecent or
offensive to the sense or an obstruction to the free use of property so as to
interfere with the comfortable enjoyment of life or property, is declared a
nuisance and as such, shall be abated.
(Prior Code, § 6-1-34)
§ 91.07 KEEPING OF JUNK RESTRICTED.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to store or keep any old articles or
materials which may be classified as junk adjacent to or in close proximity to
any school house, church, public park, public ground, business buildings, or
residences without first providing proper and tight buildings for the storage
of the same.
(Prior Code, § 6-1-27) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 91.08 WINDOWSILL TO BE KEPT CLEAR.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to place or keep on any windowsill,
porch, or other projection above the first story of any building abutting on
any sidewalk any article which might do injury by falling upon any person on
the sidewalk in front of such building, unless said article be securely
fastened or protected by screens.
(Prior Code, § 6-1-47) Penalty, see §
10.99

GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 92.01 ADOPTION OF FIRE PREVENTION CODE.
   For the purpose of regulating and governing conditions hazardous to life and
property from fire, the Fire Prevention Code, current edition, as recommended
by the National Board of Fire Underwriters, is hereby adopted. Said Fire
Prevention Code, three copies of which shall be on file at all times in the
office of the Clerk, shall be made a part of this code as if set out at length
herein.
(Prior Code, § 3-1-1)
§ 92.02 EXPLOSIVES.
   (A)   Explosives prohibited. It shall be unlawful for any person to make,
keep, or transport any gunpowder, nitroglycerin, or other highly explosive
substance.
(Prior Code, § 3-2-1)
   (B)   Exception permitted. A vehicle carrying explosives may be permitted on
the streets only if a special written permit has first been obtained from the
Chief of Police. The permit shall specify the exact route to be used by said
vehicle and may permit the vehicle to be parked at a certain specified place
for a certain specified amount of time. Each such permit shall be valid only
for the one specified use.
(Prior Code, § 3-2-2)
Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 92.03 FIREWORKS.
   (A)   Fireworks prohibited. It shall be unlawful for any person to have in
his or her possession, either for sale or for use by himself or herself, any
pyrotechnic device commonly known as fireworks, except as hereinafter set
forth.
(Prior Code, § 3-3-1)
   (B)   Exceptions. Any recognized civic or local organization may make
application to the Council for a special permit for a fireworks display to be
held in connection with a national holiday or any special local event. Such
application shall be made in writing to the Clerk, who shall present said
application to the Council for its action. The Mayor and Council shall make
such investigation as deemed necessary and may issue a permit subject to any
special provisions deemed necessary. Such permit shall not be of a continuing
nature but shall be exclusive to the one time only for which it is issued.
(Prior Code, § 3-3-2)
   (C)   Safe and sane fireworks. Sale at retail and the use of safe and sane
fireworks, as herein described, shall be lawful from June 20 through July 6 of
each year. SAFE AND SANE FIREWORKS includes any of the following:
      (1)   Cone fountains with pyrotechnic composition not exceeding 50 grams
each;
      (2)   Cylindrical fountains, whether base, spike, or handle, with
pyrotechnic composition not exceeding 75 grams each and inside tube diameter
not exceeding three-fourths inch;
      (3)   Sparklers and dipped sticks not more than ten inches in length or
one-fourth inch in diameter made on steel or iron wire and Suzuki and morning
glories with pyrotechnic composition not exceeding four grams each;
      (4)   Snakes which do not contain bichloride of mercury and pyrotechnic
composition exceeding two grams each;
      (5)   Wheels with pyrotechnic composition not exceeding 60 grains for
each driver unit or 240 grains for each complete wheel. The inside tube
diameter of driver unit shall not exceed one-half inch; and
      (6)   Whistles, without report and which do not dart or travel about the
ground during discharge, with pyrotechnic composition not exceeding six grams
and containing no picric or gallic acid.
(Prior Code, § 3-3-3)
Penalty, see §
10.99
FIRE DEPARTMENT
§ 92.15 ESTABLISHMENT.
   Any number of residents of the city, not less than ten in number and not
more than 20, may form a volunteer fire company for the protection or guarding
against fires, protecting property from fire, and extinguishing fire.
(Prior Code, § 3-6-1) (Ord. 78, passed 4-9-1912)
§ 92.16 DUTIES.
   It shall be the duty fo each member of said fire company to become
thoroughly acquainted with the firefighting apparatus in the city, and to
perform all the duties required or him or her by the Council and by the
officers of the said fire company.
(Prior Code, § 3-6-2) (Ord. 78, passed 4-9-1912)
§ 92.17 CHIEF; ELECTION.
   Said fire company shall elect from their own number a Chief, whose authority
in case of fire or in case of practice shall be supreme, and it shall be the
duty of the Fire Chief to place all members of the fire company in such
positions as he or she may deem fit for the effectual workings of said fire
company.
(Prior Code, § 3-6-3) (Ord. 78, passed 4-9-1912)
§ 92.18 PRACTICES.
   The fire company shall hold practice at least six times a year for not less
than one-half hour at each practice, and the failure of any member of the fire
company to attend five practice meetings of the fire company during any one
year shall forfeit his or her membership in the fire company.
(Prior Code, § 3-6-4) (Ord. 78, passed 4-9-1912)
§ 92.19 ASSOCIATION.
   The fire organization shall form a volunteer association with a constitution
and bylaws to be approved by the Council before such organization shall be
recognized as the fire company of the city.
(Prior Code, § 3-6-5) (Ord. 78, passed 4-9-1912)
BURNING REGULATIONS
§ 92.30 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions apply unless
the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   HEATING APPLIANCE/INCINERATOR. A burn barrel would be considered an
INCINERATOR so long as the burn barrel and surrounding area comply with the
following minimum standards: the burn barrel is no larger than a 55-gallon
barrel in good condition; has proper ventilation in the lower portion of the
barrel with each hole for ventilation that is larger in area than one square
inch being backed by metal screen; has an expanded metal screen with holes not
larger than five-eighths inch covering the top; and the area around the burn
barrel is cleared down to mineral soil or gravel at least ten feet on each side
of the INCINERATOR.
   OPEN BURNING or OPEN BURN. The igniting or combustion of any material not
contained in a heating appliance or incinerator, including, but not limited to,
campfires, cook fires, and the burning of water, refuse, or other materials.
   REFUSE. All solid wastes, garbage, and rubbish, including, but not limited
to, cardboard, plastic, rubber, Styrofoam, petroleum products, furniture,
foodstuff, or chemically treated wood.
   SOLID FUEL. Nonliquid combustible material including wood, coal, pressed
logs, pellet fuel, but excluding items defined herein as “refuse.”
   YARD WASTE. Natural yard debris, including Christmas trees, leaves, pine
needles, and tree branches.
(Prior Code, § 3-5-1) (Ord. 2021-003, passed 12-8-2021)
§ 92.31 BURNING OF RUBBISH IN BUSINESS DISTRICTS.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to burn or cause to be burned any trash,
lumber, yard waste, straw, papers, or any other combustible material outside of
any building in any street, alley, vacant lot, or vacant portion of any lot
located within the business district of the city.
(Prior Code, § 3-5-2) (Ord. 2021-003, passed 12-8-2021) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 92.32 BURNING OF RUBBISH IN RESIDENTIAL DISTRICTS.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to burn or cause to be burned any trash,
lumber, yard waste, straw, papers, or any other combustible material outside of
any building district of the city from the period of May 10 of each year to
October 20 of each year, without first obtaining a permit from the Clerk
stating when such burning shall be done and under such proper safeguards as the
Council may direct.
(Prior Code, § 3-5-3) (Ord. 2021-003, passed 12-8-2021) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 92.33 BURNING BY PERMIT.
   (A)   Permits issued. Burn permits may be issued between May 10 to October
20 of each year by the City Clerk, an individual designated by the City Clerk,
or City Council upon such terms and conditions as follows.
      (1)   There shall be no fee for a burn permit.
      (2)   Applicants shall make an application to the City Clerk, an
individual designated by the City Clerk, or City Council, on such forms as
provided by the city.
      (3)   In addition to other requirements or conditions as may be
established, the applicant may be required, in the Fire Chief’s, City Clerk’s,
or City Council’s discretion, to provide the following as a condition for
granting a permit.
         (a)   Proof of sufficient insurance or other means of financial
responsibility; and
         (b)   A plan describing the applicant’s proposed means of
extinguishment and suppression as a condition for granting a permit.
      (4)   Permits may only be issued for a maximum of five consecutive days.
      (5)   The City Council, at its discretion or upon recommendation by the
Fire Chief, may put a moratorium on the issuance of any burn permits. The City
Council may also extend the duration and modify the conditions of any burn
permit upon request of the Fire Chief, City Clerk, or applicant.
   (B)   Application denial.
      (1)   The City Clerk, or an individual designated by the City Clerk, may
deny an application if:
         (a)   The applicant fails to provide any information requested;
         (b)   Granting the permit would pose an undue risk to the safety of
persons or property;
         (c)   The applicant has been cited for violating this subchapter on
more than three occasions in one calendar year; or
         (d)   Any other reason permitted by law.
      (2)   A denial of an application shall be served in writing by certified
mail or by personal delivery to the applicant.
   (C)   Appeals. If the City Clerk denies an application, the applicant may
appeal the denial to the City Council by filing a written request for an appeal
hearing within 28 days after the date the denial was mailed.
   (D)   Variances. The City Council may grant variances to the condition
contained herein upon application from any interested party if the Council
finds that the variance would not adversely impact the health, safety, and
welfare of the citizens and if any requested variance meets the standards and
approval of the Fire Department.
(Prior Code, § 3-5-4) (Ord. 2021-003, passed 12-8-2021)
§ 92.34 EXCEPTIONS.
   Nothing in this subchapter shall prohibit the burning of combustible
materials in the Residential District in covered barrels or containers so
constructed as to prevent the escape of any burning material, and such
containers shall be subject to the approval of the Fire Chief.
(Prior Code, § 3-5-5) (Ord. 2021-003, passed 12-8-2021)
§ 92.35 OPEN BURNING.
   (A)   Open burning is allowed for garden waste, tree trimmings, and brush
only.
   (B)   The following conditions are requested for open burning.
      (1)   Burning shall be at a distance of at least 25 feet from any
building, structure, or other combustible material when the pile size is three
feet or less in diameter and two feet or less in height. Anything larger shall
be 50 feet or more from any structure or other combustible material.
      (2)   A garden hose with water supply or other fire extinguishing
equipment shall be on hand and a competent person will be at the burn site at
all times until the fire has been totally extinguished. Persons who are burning
debris must be in legal control of the lot or parcel of land on which the
burning is to take place.
      (3)   There will be no open burning on public land.
      (4)   No waste matter shall be burned which will, in the burning process,
produce toxic, dense or offensive odors.
      (5)   No burning will be allowed after dark, and persons who are burning
debris will make sure that all fires are totally extinguished before leaving
the site.
      (6)   No demolition or construction site burning is permitted burning
this burning period.
      (7)   This burning period shall not include lot burning, yard waste,
grass trimmings, or any rubbish containing paper products.
      (8)   A permit is not required for this type of burning; however, persons
who do not meet all of the above requirements may be subject to the permit
requirements of this subchapter and/or fines as per this code.
      (9)   Burning will be ordered to immediately discontinue if the Fire
Chief or his or her designee on duty determines that smoke emissions are
offensive to occupants of surrounding property, or if open burning is
determined by the City Code Officer or Fire Duty Officer to constitute a
hazardous condition, or the Department of Environmental Quality issues an air
quality forecast and caution with a mandatory burn ban.
(Prior Code, § 3-5-6) (Ord. 2021-003, passed 12-8-2021) Penalty, see §
10.99
CHAPTER 93: PARKS AND RECREATION
Section
Latah Trail
   
93.01   Horses and unauthorized motor vehicles prohibited

LATAH TRAIL
§ 93.01 HORSES AND UNAUTHORIZED MOTOR VEHICLES PROHIBITED.
   No person shall ride or allow to be ridden horses or drive or allow to be
driven any unauthorized motor vehicle on the portion of the Latah Trail located
within the city limits, which is also known as the Clint Illi Walkway.
(Prior Code, § 7-10-1) (Ord. 2012-01, passed 6-13-2012) Penalty, see §
93.99
§ 93.02 CAMPING ALLOWED IN DESIGNATED AREAS ONLY.
   Camping shall be allowed, by permit only, in designated areas along the
Latah Trail located within the city limits. The City Council shall adopt by
resolution the fees, rules, and regulations for applications for camping
permits, as well as the boundaries of the designated areas, provided that said
camping permits shall be valid for no more than three consecutive days without
prior approval from the City Council.
(Prior Code, § 7-10-2) (Ord. 2012-01, passed 6-13-2012) Penalty, see §
93.99
§ 93.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code of ordinances.
   (B)   A violation of §§
93.01 or
93.02 shall be an infraction as defined in Idaho Code § 18-111, punishable by a
penalty not to exceed $100, and for which no period of incarceration may be
imposed. The City Council shall set the penalty for this violation by
resolution of the Council.
(Prior Code, § 7-10-3) (Ord. 2012-01, passed 6-13-2012)

CHAPTER 110: GENERAL BUSINESS REGULATIONS

GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 110.01 BILLPOSTING AND HANDBILLS.
   (A)   License required. It shall be unlawful for any person to engage in the
distribution or attaching of any signs, bills, pictures, or advertising matter
unless the person shall first have obtained a license therefor.
(Prior Code, § 5-2-1)
   (B)   Application. Application for a license shall be made to the Clerk,
together with all necessary information, including, but not limited to, the
names of all owners and the business addresses of the same. Upon approval of
said application by the Council, the Clerk shall issue a license for which a
fee of $25 per annum shall be paid.
(Prior Code, § 5-2-2)
   (C)   Littering public thoroughfares. It shall be unlawful for any person to
scatter or throw upon the public thoroughfares any handbills, posters,
advertisements, or papers. Nothing herein shall be construed to authorize any
person to obstruct the public thoroughfares or prevent the posting of notices
required by law to be posted.
(Prior Code, § 5-2-3)
   (D)   No posting on fences; telegraph poles. It shall be unlawful for any
person to post, paint, tack, or otherwise attach any notice or other
advertising matter to any fence, wall, or building or other property until
first obtaining the consent of the owner of such property. It shall be unlawful
for any person to post, paint, tack, or otherwise attach any notices or
advertising matter to any telegraph, telephone, electric, or other such poles.
(Prior Code, § 5-2-4)
Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 110.02 ADOPTION OF U.S. PUBLIC HEALTH SERVICE ORDINANCE.
   (A)   The inspection, grading, regrading, and placarding of eating and
drinking establishments within the municipality, or its police jurisdiction,
the issuing, suspension, and revocation of permits for the operation of such
establishments, the sale of adulterated, misbranded, or unwholesome food and
drink, and the enforcement of this section shall be regulated in accordance
with the terms of the unabridged form of the 1943 Edition of the U.S. Public
Health Service ordinance regulating eating and drinking establishments, three
certified copies of which shall be on file in the office of the Clerk;
provided, however, that in § 2 of said U.S. Public Health Service ordinance,
itinerant restaurants shall be required to secure a permit.
   (B)   Provided further that when any restaurant fails to qualify for any of
the grades specified in the U.S. Public Health Service ordinance, the health
officer or other designated official is authorized to suspend the permit, or in
lieu thereof, to degrade the restaurant and permit its operation during a
temporary period not exceeding 30 days.
(Prior Code, § 4-1-1)
§ 110.03 MILK.
   (A)   Adoption of Public Health Service Milk Code. The production and
handling of milk and milk products sold for ultimate consumption within the
municipality, or its jurisdiction, all inspections, the issuing and revoking of
permits, and the serving of milk to the public shall be regulated by the
adoption of the U.S. Public Health Service Milk Code, published by the U.S.
Department of Health, Education, and Welfare (1953), being 21 C.F.R. part 131,
three copies of which are now on file in the office of the Clerk, and said code
is hereby adopted and incorporated as if fully set out at length herein.
(Prior Code, § 4-2-1)
   (B)   Permits. Under § 3 of the code adopted in division (A) above, permits
issued shall be in the sum of $25 per year, payable in advance.
(Prior Code, § 4-2-2)
LICENSES
§ 110.15 APPLICATION.
   (A)   Applications for all licenses and permits required by this code shall
be made in writing to the Clerk, unless otherwise specifically provided by law.
   (B)   Each application shall state the name of the applicant, the permit or
license desired, the location to be used, if any, the time covered, and the fee
to be paid. Each application shall contain such additional information as may
be required by the issuing official.
(Prior Code, § 5-1-1)
§ 110.16 PERSON SUBJECT TO LICENSE.
   Whenever in this code a license is required for the maintenance, operation,
or conduct of any business or establishment, or for doing business or engaging
in any activity or occupation, any person or corporation shall be subject to
the requirement if by himself or herself or through an agent, employee, or
partner, he or she holds himself forth as being engaged in the business or
occupation; or solicits patronage therefor, actively or passively; or performs
or attempts to perform any part of such business or occupation.
(Prior Code, § 5-1-2)
§ 110.17 FORMS.
   Forms of all licenses and permits, and applications therefor, shall be
prepared and kept on file by the Clerk.
(Prior Code, § 5-1-3)
§ 110.18 SIGNATURES.
   Each license or permit issued, in the absence of any provision to the
contrary, shall bear the signatures of the Mayor and the Clerk.
(Prior Code, § 5-1-4)
§ 110.19 INVESTIGATIONS.
   Upon the receipt of an application for a license or permit where laws of the
city necessitate an inspection or investigation before the issuance of such
permit or license, the Clerk shall refer such application to the proper officer
for making such investigation within 48 hours of the time of such receipt. The
officer charged with the duty of making the investigation or inspection shall
make a report thereon, favorable or otherwise, within ten days after receiving
the application or a copy thereof. The health officer or other designated
official shall make or cause to be made an inspection in regard to such
licenses in the connection of the care and handling of food and the preventing
of nuisances and the spread of disease. For the protection of health, the
Building Inspector shall make or cause to be made any such inspection relative
to the construction of buildings or other structures. All other investigations,
except where otherwise provided, shall be made by the Chief of Police or by
some other officer designated by the Mayor.
(Prior Code, § 5-1-5)
§ 110.20 TERMINATION OF LICENSE.
   (A)   All annual licenses shall terminate on the last day of the fiscal year
of the municipality where no provision to the contrary is made.
   (B)   The Clerk shall mail to all licensees of the municipality a statement
of the time of expiration of the license held by the licensee, if an annual,
three weeks prior to the date of such expiration; provided, that failure to
send out such notice, or failure of the licencee to receive it, shall not
excuse the licensee from failure to obtain a new license, or a renewal thereof,
nor shall it be a defense in an action for operation without a license.
(Prior Code, § 5-1-6)
§ 110.21 BUILDING AND PREMISES.
   No license shall be issued for the conduct of any business, and no permit
shall be issued for any thing, or act, if the premises and building to be used
for the purpose does not fully comply with the requirements of this code. No
such license or permit shall be issued for the conduct of any business or
performance of any act which would involve a violation of the zoning act of the
municipality.
(Prior Code, § 5-1-7)
§ 110.22 CHANGE OF LOCATION.
   In the absence of any provision to the contrary, the location of any
licensed business or occupation, or of any permitted act, may be changed;
provided, that application for such change is made to the Council and the
Council, by majority vote, approves such change; provided, the building,
zoning, and frontage consent requirements of this code are complied with.
(Prior Code, § 5-1-8)
§ 110.23 FRONTAGE CONSENTS.
   (A)   Whenever the consent of the adjoining or neighboring owners is
required as a prerequisite to the conduct of any business or occupation, or the
location of any establishment, such consent must be obtained by securing the
necessary signatures to a written consent petition. Such petition shall be
filed with the Clerk when signed.
   (B)   Consents, once given and filed, shall not be withdrawn, and such
petitions need not be renewed for the continuous conduct of the same business,
whether by the same proprietor or not.
   (C)   It shall be unlawful to forge any name to such a petition or to
represent falsely that the names thereon have been properly placed thereon if
such is not the fact.
   (D)   Each consent, when filed, shall be accompanied by the affidavit of the
person securing the signatures that each signature appearing therein was
properly secured and written on, and that the petition contains the necessary
number of signatures required by this code.
   (E)   The frontage consent requirements contained in this code shall not be
construed to amend or change any zoning provision of the municipality, and no
such provision shall be construed as permitting the erection of a structure or
building, or the conduct of a business or the commission of any act in any
location where such structure, building, business, or act is or are prohibited
by any zoning law of the municipality.
(Prior Code, § 5-1-9) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 110.24 NUISANCES.
   No business, licensed or not, shall be so conducted or operated as to amount
to a nuisance in fact.
(Prior Code, § 5-1-10) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 110.25 INSPECTIONS.
   (A)   Whenever inspections of the premises used for or in connection with
the operation of a licensed business or occupation are provided for or required
by this code, or are reasonably necessary to secure compliance with any code
provision or to detect violations thereof, it shall be the duty of the
licensee, or the person in charge of the premises to be inspected, to admit
thereto for the purpose of making the inspection any officer or employee of the
city who is authorized or directed to make such inspection at any reasonable
time that admission is requested. Whenever an analysis of any commodity or
material is reasonably necessary to secure conformance with any code provision
or to detect violations thereof, it shall be the duty of the licensee whose
business is governed by such provision to give to any authorized officer or
employee of the city requesting the same sufficient samples of such material or
commodity for such analysis upon request.
   (B)   In addition to any other penalty which may be provided, the Council
may revoke the license of any licensed business in the city whose proprietor or
owner refuses to permit any such officer or employee who is authorized to make
such inspection or take such sample to make the inspection, or take an adequate
sample of the said commodity, or who interferes with such officer or employee
while in the performance of his or her duty in making such inspection;
provided, that no license shall be revoked for such cause unless written demand
is made upon the licensee or person in charge of the premises, in the name of
the city, stating that such inspection or sample is desired at the time it is
sought to make the inspection or obtain the sample.
(Prior Code, § 5-1-11)
§ 110.26 REVOCATION.
   Any license or permit issued for a limited time may be revoked by the Mayor
at any time for any violation, the subject matter of the license or permit, or
to the premises occupied. Such revocation may be in addition to any fine
imposed.
(Prior Code, § 5-1-12)
§ 110.27 POSTING OF LICENSE.
   It shall be the duty of any person conducting a licensed business in the
city to keep his or her license posted at all times in a prominent place on the
premises used for such business.
(Prior Code, § 5-1-13) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 110.28 FEES.
   (A)   In the absence of specific provisions to the contrary, all fees and
charges for licenses or permits shall be paid to the Clerk, in advance at the
time application therefor is made. When an applicant has not engaged in the
business until after the expiration of more than six months of the current
license year, the license fee shall be in the sum of one-half of the fee
specified for the entire year. All license fees shall be deposited in the
General Fund.
   (B)   Licenses shall be required for the following activities and businesses
upon payment of the fee indicated for the specified time:
      (1)   Amusements:
         (a)   Carnivals: $100 per week;
         (b)   Exhibitions of inanimate objects: $5 per day;
         (c)   Menageries: $5 per day; and
         (d)   Other amusements: $10 per day.
      (2)   Auctioneers: $5 per day;
      (3)   Music boxes: $10 annually; and
      (4)   Public dances: $15 per day or $100 annually.
(Prior Code, § 5-1-14)
CHAPTER 111: SOLICITORS
Section
   
111.01   Definitions
   
111.02   License application

111.99   Penalty
§ 111.01 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions apply unless the
context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   HAWKER. Any person who offers goods, wares, or merchandise of any kind at
outcry upon any street or vacant lot in the city, whether by auction of
otherwise.
   PEDDLER. Any person who goes from house to house and offers for sales goods,
wares, or merchandise of any kind or description carried with him or her taking
orders for future delivery of goods, wares, or merchandise of any kind or
description.
(Prior Code, § 5-6-1)
§ 111.02 LICENSE APPLICATION.
   Application for a license to be issued under the provisions of this chapter
shall be made to the Clerk and shall contain a statement containing the type of
business contemplated.
(Prior Code, § 5-6-2)
§ 111.03 FEE.
   A license fee shall be paid by hawkers and peddlers of $10 per day, $100 per
month, or $500 per year, unless otherwise provided in this chapter.
(Prior Code, § 5-6-3)
§ 111.04 BOND REQUIRED.
   (A)   Every applicant shall file with the Clerk a surety bond running to the
municipality in the amount of $1,000, with the surety acceptable to and
approved by the Mayor, conditioned that the said applicant shall comply fully
with all the provisions of this chapter.
   (B)   Action on such bond may be brought in the name of the municipality to
the use and benefit of the aggrieved person.
(Prior Code, § 5-6-4) Penalty, see §
111.99
§ 111.05 DISPLAY OF LICENSE.
   Any hawker or peddler is required to exhibit his or her license upon the
request of any citizen or police officer.
(Prior Code, § 5-6-5) Penalty, see §
111.99
§ 111.06 REVOCATION OF LICENSE.
   Licenses issued under the provisions of this chapter may be revoked by the
Mayor for any of the following causes:
   (A)   Fraud, misrepresentation, or false statement contained in the
application for license;
   (B)   Fraud, misrepresentation, or false statement made in the course of
carrying on a business;
   (C)   Any violation of this chapter; or
   (D)   Conducting the business in an unlawful manner or in such a manner as
to constitute a breach of the peace or to constitute a menace to the health,
safety, or general welfare of the public.
(Prior Code, § 5-6-6)
§ 111.07 PEDDLERS A NUISANCE.
   The practice of going in and upon private residences in the city by
unlicensed solicitors, unlicensed peddlers, unlicensed hawkers, unlicensed
transient merchants, and unlicensed transient vendors of merchandise, not
having been requested or invited so to do by the owner of said private
residence, for the purpose of soliciting orders for the sale or future delivery
of goods, wares, and merchandise of any kind or description, and/or for the
purpose of disposing and/or peddling or hawking the same, is hereby declared to
be a nuisance.
(Prior Code, § 5-6-7) Penalty, see §
111.99
§ 111.08 DUTY OF POLICE TO ENFORCE.
   It shall be the duty of any police officer to enforce the provisions of this
chapter.
(Prior Code, § 5-6-8)
§ 111.09 AGRICULTURAL SALES EXCEPTED.
   Nothing in this chapter shall be construed to require a license or prohibit
the door to door selling of agricultural products grown or produced within the
state.
(Prior Code, § 5-6-10)
§ 111.10 REDUCTION OF FEES.
   (A)   The Mayor and/or Council shall have authority to reduce the license
fee for hawkers, peddlers, or salespersons to $3 per three-month period in any
of the following instances:
      (1)   When the applicant is a resident of the city;
      (2)   When the applicant owns and/or operates a business in the city;
      (3)   When the applicant represents a civic organization and the funds
derived from such hawking or peddling are used for charitable purposes; or
      (4)   When the applicant is engaged in selling books, encyclopedias,
bibles, or religious materials and the sale of such materials is deemed by the
Mayor and/or Council to be in the public interest.
   (B)   In all cases, the decision of the Mayor and/or Council in the amount
of the fee shall be final.
(Prior Code, § 5-6-11)
§ 111.99 PENALTY.
   Any apparent violation of this chapter shall be punishable by the provisions
of this code.
(Prior Code, § 5-6-9)
