LIQUOR BY THE DRINK
§ 112.01 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions apply unless
the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   LICENSE. Unless the context shows otherwise, a license issued by the city to
a qualified person or corporation under which it shall be lawful for the
licensee to sell and dispense liquor by the drink at retail, as provided by the
laws of the state.
   LICENSED PREMISES. A qualified premises for which a license has been issued
by the city.
   QUALIFIED APPLICANT. A person or corporation having a currently valid
license from the Commission of Law Enforcement of the state to sell liquor by
the drink at a location in the city in accordance with the provisions of laws
of the state.
   QUALIFIED PREMISES. A restaurant as defined and by this subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 5-8-1) (Ord. passed 1- -1968)
§ 112.02 LICENSE TO RETAIL LIQUOR.
   (A)   The Clerk is hereby empowered, authorized, and directed to issue
licenses to qualified applicants, as herein provided, for qualified premises
whereby the licensee shall be authorized and permitted to sell liquor by the
drink at retail at such qualified premises in the city. Upon the issue of such
license, the licensee therein named shall be authorized to sell liquor by the
drink at the qualified premises, but only in accordance with the provisions of
laws of the state and the rules and regulations promulgated by the Commissioner
of Law Enforcement of the state in regard thereto and the provisions of this
subchapter.
   (B)   No person or corporation shall sell or dispense liquor by the drink at
any location within the corporate limits of the city without first having
obtained a license therefor from the city in accordance with the terms of this
subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 5-8-2) (Ord. passed 1- -1968) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 112.03 LICENSE FEE.
   Each licensee before being licensed by the city under the provisions of this
subchapter shall pay an annual license fee to the Clerk in the sum of $225 per
annum; and it is expressly provided that such license fee shall not be prorated
for any portion of a year less than an entire year. The license fee herein
provided for is exclusive and in addition to other license fees chargeable by
the city.
(Prior Code, § 5-8-3) (Ord. passed 1- -1968)
§ 112.04 APPLICATION FOR LICENSE.
   (A)   Prior to the issuance of a license as herein provided, the applicant
shall file with the Clerk an application in writing, signed by the applicant
or, if the applicant be a corporation, by one of its officers, containing such
information and statements relative to the applicant and the premises where
liquor by the drink is to be sold as may be required by the Clerk, and
accompanied by the license issued to the applicant by the Department of Law
Enforcement of the state to sell liquor by the drink in the city.
   (B)   The application shall be verified by the affidavit of the person or
corporation making the same before a person authorized to administer oaths, and
shall be accompanied with the license fee herein required.
   (C)   If any false statement is made in such application, the applicant
shall be deemed to have violated the provisions of this subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 5-8-4) (Ord. passed 1- -1968)
§ 112.05 FORM OF LICENSES; AUTHORITY; EXPIRATION.
   (A)   Every license issued under the provisions of this subchapter shall set
forth the name of the person or corporation to whom issued, the location by
street and number or other definite designation, of the qualified premises to
be licensed, and such other reasonable information as the Clerk shall deem
necessary. If issued to a partnership, the names and addresses of the persons
constituting such partnership shall be set forth. If issued to a corporation or
association, the names and addresses of the principal officers shall be set
forth. Such license shall be signed by the licensee and shall not be
transferable except upon the express consent of the Mayor and Council.
   (B)   Every license issued under this provision of this subchapter is
separate and distinct, and no person except the licensee therein named shall
exercise any of the privileges granted thereunder, and all licenses are
applicable only to the qualified premises in respect to which they are issued.
Unless sooner revoked or suspended, all licenses shall expire at 1:00 a.m. on
January 1 of the year following the date of issue. No person or corporation
shall be granted more than one license in the city for any one year.
   (C)   The Clerk shall issue no license within the meaning of this chapter to
any applicant without the formal approval of the Mayor and Council, and the
Mayor and Council shall approve no licenses, or the issuance thereof, to more
than two licensees so long as the population of the city is less than 1,500.
(Prior Code, § 5-8-5) (Ord. passed 1- -1968)
§ 112.06 HOURS OF SALE OF LIQUOR.
   No liquor by the drink shall be sold, offered for sale, given away, or
consumed upon any licensed premises during the following hours:
   (A)   Christmas from 1:00 a.m. to 10:00 a.m. the following day;
   (B)   On any other day between 1:00 a.m. and 10:00 a.m.; or
   (C)    On the day of a general or primary election until after the time when
the polls are closed.
(Prior Code, § 5-8-6) (Ord. passed 1- -1968; Ord. 255, passed - -1986) Penalty,
see §
10.99
§ 112.07 DAYS FOR SALE OF LIQUOR EXTENDED.
   Under the authority to extend the hours when liquor may be sold and to
increase the days on which liquor may be sold as expressed in Idaho Code § 23-
927(2), as presently in effect or as may hereafter be amended, and under the
same authority expressed in County Ordinance 84, the city hereby declares that
the hours during which liquor may be sold are not extended and Idaho Code § 23-
927(1)(a) shall remain in effect as to the hours when liquor may be sold and
that the days on which liquor may be sold are hereby increased to include
Sundays, Memorial Day, and Thanksgiving Day.
(Prior Code, § 5-8-6-1) (Ord. 255, passed - -1986)
§ 112.08 TERMINATION OF LICENSES; REVOCATION.
   Revocation of the license issued to any licensee by the state shall
automatically be and become a revocation of the license of such licensee issued
by the city.
(Prior Code, § 5-8-7) (Ord. passed 1- -1968)
§ 112.09 SUSPENSION OF LICENSE.
   Suspension of the license issued to any licensee by the state shall
automatically be and become a suspension of the license of the licensee issued
by the city for the period of suspension of the license issued by the state.
(Prior Code, § 5-8-8) (Ord. passed 1- -1968)
§ 112.10 MINORS.
   No person shall sell, serve, or dispense liquor by the drink to any person
under the age of 21 years.
(Prior Code, § 5-8-9) (Ord. passed 1- -1968) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 112.11 EMPLOYEES.
   Any violation of any of the provisions of this subchapter by any agent,
employee, servant, or other person acting in behalf of the licensee, shall be
presumed to be a violation by the licensee.
(Prior Code, § 5-8-10) (Ord. passed 1- -1968)
§ 112.12 INSPECTION.
   Any police officer of the city, or of the county or the state, shall have
the right at any time to make inspections and examinations of any premises
licensed under this subchapter to sell liquor by the drink as to whether the
provisions of this code and the laws of the state are being complied with, and
any applicant for a license under this subchapter shall be deemed to have
consented to such inspection and examination.
(Prior Code, § 5-8-11) (Ord. passed 1- -1968)
§ 112.13 RESTAURANT RESTRICTION.
   (A)   (1)   Notwithstanding anything herein contained to the contrary, no
license for the sale of liquor by the drink in the city shall be issued under
this subchapter, or otherwise, to any applicant for any premises unless the
premises shall qualify as a restaurant, as defined in this section. A
RESTAURANT, within the meaning of this subchapter, shall mean, and is hereby
defined to be, an establishment having a kitchen and kitchen facilities for the
preparation of hot meals, and where, in consideration for payment, hot meals
are regularly prepared and served to the public on the premises for consumption
on the premises. Fry orders, short orders, sandwiches, salads, hamburgers, and
hot dogs shall not be deemed MEALS within the provisions of this chapter.
      (2)   Any establishment for which a license is issued under this chapter
shall remain qualified as a restaurant, as defined in this section, at all
times during the period for which the license is issued. If at any time during
any period for which a license is issued under this subchapter, the premises
for which the license is issued fails to meet the qualifications of a
restaurant, as defined in this section, the license issued for such premises
shall be revoked by order of the Council or suspended until such premises again
meets the qualifications of a restaurant, as defined in this section.
      (3)   In order for any establishment to remain qualified as a restaurant,
as defined in this section, during a license period, the gross receipts of such
establishment from the sale and service of food for consumption on the premises
shall, from calendar month to calendar month, exceed 50% of the total gross
receipts of such establishment. If during any consecutive two calendar month
period the gross receipts of such establishment from the sale and service of
food on the premises does not exceed 50% of the gross receipts of such
establishment for such two calendar month period, such establishment shall not
be deemed a qualified premises for a license.
   (B)   The provisions of this section may be waived by a majority vote of the
full City Council upon a showing that there is no restaurant in the city which
desires to, and is capable of, assuming said license.
(Prior Code, § 5-8-12) (Ord. 265, passed 9-6-1988) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 112.14 COMPLIANCE DURING LICENSE PERIOD.
   A licensee and the licensed premises must continue throughout the license
period to have all of the foregoing qualifications. If the licensee or licensed
premises should fail to have all of the foregoing qualifications at any time
during the license period, the Council shall revoke the license of the
licensee, or shall suspend the license of the licensee until the licenses and
licensed premises shall again meet the qualifications of this subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 5-8-13) (Ord. passed 1- -1968)
§ 112.15 REVOCATION OR SUSPENSION.
   The Council may revoke, or suspend, any license issued under this subchapter
if, upon a hearing thereof after at least ten days’ notice given to the
licensee by personal service on the licensee, or by mail addressed to the
licensee at the address shown on the licensee’s application for a license, or
left with an adult employee of the licensee on the licensed premises, the
Council finds that the licensee, or his or her agent or employee, has violated
or neglected to comply with any of the provisions of this subchapter, or has on
the licensed premises violated any of the laws of the state pertaining to the
sale of beer or intoxicating beverages or prohibiting gambling, or has made any
false statement in the application for such license or transfer thereof, or did
not have, or has not maintained the qualifications of a licensee, or had, or
has acquired, a disqualification of a licensee, or whose licensed premises is
not qualified as a restaurant within the definition contained in this
subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 5-8-14) (Ord. passed 1- -1968)
§ 112.16 RECORDS.
   (A)   (1)   The city shall have the right at all times to inspect and
examine the books and records of any applicant for a license or licensee under
this subchapter.
      (2)   Any licensee shall, upon request of the city, forthwith submit and
file with the city financial statements setting forth and showing thereon the
percentage of the licensee’s gross receipts from the sale and service of food
for consumption on the licensed premises and from other sources. Such financial
statements shall cover the period of time requested by the city; provided, that
such period shall not be more than six consecutive calendar months immediately
preceding the request made by the city.
   (B)   If any false statement or entry is contained in any such financial
statement, or in the books or records of the licensee, the licensee shall be
deemed to have violated the provisions of this subchapter.
   (C)   An application for, and acceptance by a licensee of, a license under
this chapter shall constitute consent to and authority for the city to enter
upon the licensed premises and to inspect the licensee’s books and records. The
licensee’s records and books shall be kept at and on the licensed premises. A
licensee shall, if requested by the city, cause its books and records to be
audited by a certified public accountant and to cause the financial statements
mentioned in division (A)(2) above to be prepared and certified by a certified
public accountant.
(Prior Code, § 5-8-15) (Ord. passed 1- -1968) Penalty, see §
10.99
WINE
§ 112.30 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions apply unless the
context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   COMMISSIONER. The Commissioner of Law Enforcement of the state.
   PERSON. Includes an individual, firm, copartnership, association,
corporation, or any group or combination acting as a unit, and includes the
plural as well as the singular, unless the intent to give a more limited
meaning is disclosed by the context in which it is used.
   RETAIL WINE LICENSE. A license issued by the Commissioner, authorizing a
person to sell wine at retail.
   RETAILER. A person to whom a retail wine license or a wine by the drink
license has been issued.
   WINE. Any alcoholic beverage containing not more than 14% alcohol by volume
obtained by the fermentation of the natural sugar content of fruits or other
agricultural products containing sugar.
   WINE BY THE DRINK LICENSE. A license to sell wine by the individual glass or
opened bottle at retail, for consumption on the premises only.
(Prior Code, § 5-10-1) (Ord. 199, passed 7-6-1971; Ord. 212, passed 9-4-1973)
§ 112.31 LICENSE REQUIRED.
   It shall be lawful for any person to sell wine at retail within the
corporate limits of the city after having first procured the proper license
therefor.
(Prior Code, § 5-10-2) (Ord. 212, passed 9-4-1973)
§ 112.32 APPLICATION FOR LICENSE.
   Application for license shall be in writing, signed and sworn to by the
applicant upon application forms furnished by the Clerk. Such application shall
be filed by the Clerk and presented to the Mayor and Council at the next
meeting of the Council for their approval, rejection, or further consideration.
(Prior Code, § 5-10-3) (Ord. 199, passed 7-6-1971)
§ 112.33 QUALIFICATIONS.
   The applicant for a license shall possess all of the qualifications
necessary to obtain a license from the Commissioner of Law Enforcement of the
state, as prescribed by the laws of the state, and maintain such qualifications
throughout the period for which such license is issued. The possession of
licenses regularly issued by the Department of Law Enforcement and the county,
in addition to a city beer license, as provided in §§
112.55 through
112.69, shall be prima facie evidence of the applicant’s qualifications to
receive a license hereunder.
(Prior Code, § 5-10-4) (Ord. 199, passed 7-6-1971)
§ 112.34 LICENSE FEES.
   The license fee imposed and collected for the retail wine license shall be
the sum of $25 per year. The license fee imposed and collected for the wine by
the drink license shall be the sum of $25 per year. Such license year shall be
from 12:01 a.m. January 1 through December 31.
(Prior Code, § 5-10-5) (Ord. 212, passed 9-4-1973)
§ 112.35 ISSUANCE OF LICENSE.
   Upon filing the application for a license and production of evidence as
required by §
112.33 as to the qualifications of the applicant and by the payment of the
required license fee, the Clerk shall, upon approval of the Council, issue to
the applicant, depending upon the license requested, a license to sell wine at
retail and/or a license to sell wine by the drink at retail within the
municipality for such calendar year.
(Prior Code, § 5-10-6) (Ord. 212, passed 9-4-1973)
§ 112.36 LICENSE NONTRANSFERABLE.
   No license issued hereunder may be transferred from one person to another,
either by contract or operation of law, or from one location to another,
without the consent of the Council, in writing, spread on the minutes of a
regular or special meeting of the Council.
(Prior Code, § 5-10-7) (Ord. 199, passed 7-6-1971)
§ 112.37 CONSUMPTION ON PREMISES.
   Retailers who do not possess a valid license for the retail sale of liquor
by the drink or a valid wine by the drink license shall not permit consumption
of wine on the licensed premises and may sell the wine only in its original
unbroken, sealed container. Wine sold for consumption on the retailer’s
premises may be sold only during hours that beer may be sold for consumption on
the premises pursuant to the official code.
(Prior Code, § 5-10-8) (Ord. 212, passed 9-4-1973) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 112.38 POSSESSION.
   No person may, while operating or riding in or upon a motor vehicle upon a
public highway or street of this state, have in his or her possession any wine
in an open or unsealed container of any kind.
(Prior Code, § 5-10-9) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 112.39 MISREPRESENTATION OF AGE.
   (A)   No person under the age of 19 years may purchase, consume, or possess
wine.
   (B)   No person shall give, sell, or deliver wine to any person under the
age of 19 years.
   (C)   No person under the age of 19 years shall by any means represent to
any retailer or distributor that he or she is 19 years or more of age for the
purpose of inducing such retailer or distributor, or his or her agent or
employee, to sell, serve, or dispense wine to such other person.
   (D)   No person shall, by any means, represent to any retailer or
distributor or the agent or employee of such retailer or distributor, that any
other person is 19 years or more of age, when in fact such other person is
under the age of 19 years, for the purpose of inducing such retailer or
distributor, or the agent or employee of such retailer or distributor, to sell,
serve, or dispense wine to such other person.
(Prior Code, § 5-10-10) (Ord. 212, passed 9-4-1973) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 112.40 REVOCATION OF LICENSE.
   The right shall be and remain at all times vested in the Mayor and Council,
and the Mayor and Council may, as hereinafter provided, revoke or cancel any
license for fraud or misrepresentation in its procurement, or for a violation
of any of the provisions of this chapter, or for any conduct or act of the
licensee or his or her employees or any conduct or act permitted by him, her,
or them on the premises where such business is conducted, or in connection
therewith or adjacent thereto, tending to render such business on such premises
where the same is conducted as a public nuisance or a menace to the health,
peace, safety, or general welfare of the city; provided, that revocation or
suspension of the state license by the Commission of Law Enforcement shall be
deemed prima facie evidence for revocation or suspension of the license issued
herein.
(Prior Code, § 5-10-11) (Ord. 199, passed 7-6-1971)
BEER
§ 112.55 SHORT TITLE.
   This subchapter shall be known and designated as the “Beer Ordinance.”
(Prior Code, § 5-7-1) (Ord. 162, passed 7-1-1958)
§ 112.56 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions apply unless
the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   BEER. Any beverage obtained by the alcoholic fermentation of an infusion or
decoction of barley, malt, and/or other ingredients in water.
   BEER PARLOR. Any retail establishment, other than a bona fide restaurant, as
defined in this section, where, beer is sold or served for consumption on the
licensed premises.
   LICENSEE. The person or persons to whom any license is issued under the
provisions of this subchapter.
   PERSON. Includes any individual, copartnership, association, corporation, or
any group acting as a unit, and the plural as well as the singular number,
unless the intent to give a more limited meaning is disclosed by the context.
   PLACE. Any room or any premises licensed for the sale of beer for
consumption on the premises wherein there is a bar, and bar supplies and
equipment are kept, and where beer is drawn, or poured, or served for
consumption therein.
   RESTAURANT. An eating establishment having a kitchen with kitchen and
cooking facilities for the cooking and preparation of hot meals and where
complete hot meals are regularly and habitually sold and served to the public
on the premises at all times and hours during which beer is sold or served for
consumption on the premises and whose principal business is the selling and
serving of meals rather than the selling and serving of beer. Fry orders, short
orders, eggs, sandwiches and salads, and victuals of like nature, shall not be
considered MEALS with the provisions of this subchapter.
   RETAILER. Any person engaged in the sale or distribution of beer to the
consumer.
(Prior Code, § 5-7-2) (Ord. 162, passed 7-1-1958)
§ 112.57 LICENSE REQUIRED; DISPLAY.
   (A)   No person shall sell or distribute beer at any location within the
corporate limits of the city without first having obtained a license therefor
for each such location, in accordance with the terms of this subchapter.
   (B)   Such license to sell beer shall at all times be prominently displayed
in a conspicuous place in the place of business of the licensee.
(Prior Code, § 5-7-3) (Ord. 162, passed 7-1-1958) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 112.58 NUMBER OF BEER PARLORS ALLOWED.
   The number of beer parlors in the city shall be invited to one beer parlor
for each 250 valid and bona fide residents of the city, and the basis for
calculation therefor shall be the last census of the United States government.
(Prior Code, § 5-7-4) (Ord. 162, passed 7-1-1958)
§ 112.59 LICENSE FEES.
   (A)   The license fee for any retailer selling bottled or canned beer only
not for consumption on the premises where sold, shall be $25 per year.
   (B)   The license fee for any retailer selling bottled or canned beer only
for consumption on the premises where sold shall be $50 per year.
   (C)   The license fee for any retailer selling draft beer only, or draft,
bottled, and/or canned beer, shall be $100 per year.
   (D)   All beer licenses issued hereunder shall expire on December 31 of the
year in which they are issued. All license fees shall be paid in advance prior
to the issuance of the license.
(Prior Code, § 5-7-5) (Ord. 162, passed 7-1-1958)
§ 112.60 QUALIFICATIONS FOR LICENSE.
   (A)   No license to sell beer shall be issued to any applicant for such
license, or for a transfer of such license, or for the transfer thereof to any
transferee, who, or the executor, administrator, or trustee in bankruptcy of
the estate of whom:
      (1)   Is not the bona fide owner of such business, or is not a citizen of
the United States, or has not been a bona fide resident of the state for a
period of one year prior to the date of application; provided, that if the
applicant is a partnership, all partners shall be such citizens, and at least
one thereof, or the actual active manager therefor, shall have been such
resident, and if the applicant is a corporation, such corporation shall be
qualified to do business within the state, and the manager of such business
place shall be such citizen and shall have been such resident;
      (2)   Has, or any partner or actual manager or officer or employee or
spouse of which has, within three years immediately preceding such application,
been convicted of a violation of any law of the state or of the United States
of America, or of any other state regulating, governing, or prohibiting the
sale of alcoholic beverages or intoxicating liquor, or has within three years
forfeited, or suffered the forfeiture of, a bond for his or her appearance to
answer charges of any such violation;
      (3)   Has, or any partner or actual active manager or officer of which
has been convicted of any felony within five years or has paid any fine or
completed any sentence of confinement therefor within five years; or
      (4)   Has, or any partner or actual active manager or officer of which
has, within three years been convicted of any law of the state, or of the
United States, or of any other state, prohibiting gambling.
   (B)   A licensee must continue throughout the license period to have all of
the foregoing qualifications and none of the foregoing disqualifications, and
for failure therein, upon proof thereof to the Council, such Council shall
revoke the license issued.
(Prior Code, § 5-7-6) (Ord. 162, passed 7-1-1958)
§ 112.61 APPLICATION.
   (A)   Licenses required under this subchapter shall be issued by the Clerk,
who shall issue such licenses only with the approval and under the direction of
the Council. No license shall be issued except by resolution of the Council
spread upon its minutes.
   (B)   Applications for such licenses shall be made in writing, verified
under oath, and shall contain the following:
      (1)   The name, age, and residence of the applicant, and whether the
applicant is a citizen of the United States;
      (2)   A statement that the applicant has been a bona fide resident of the
state for a period of one year prior to the date of application;
      (3)   The legal description and street address of the premises on which
beer is to be sold;
      (4)   A statement showing each and every criminal offense of which the
applicant has been convicted within the ten-year period immediately preceding
the date of the application, and the time and place of such conviction or
convictions;
      (5)   The name and address of the owner and lessee of the business and of
the real property on which beer is to be sold, the manager in charge of such
business, and of each and every person employed in said business;
      (6)   The name and address of each and every person who has any monetary
or financial interest in the said business, and any mortgagee, pledgee, or
other person having any encumbrance thereon;
      (7)   The applicant consents that the police officers of the state, the
county, and of the city may inspect the premises on which such beer is to be
sold, and any portion thereof, at any time;
      (8)   The applicant agrees, during the term of his or her license, to
inform the city in writing of any change in the circumstances surrounding said
business which would in any way modify his or her representations contained in
his or her application for license, it being the intention of the city to at
all times be informed in writing as to the matters set forth in said
application; and if the place for which the license is requested is a
restaurant, a statement that such place has a kitchen and kitchen and cooking
facilities for the preparation of hot meals and that complete hot meals will
therein be regularly and habitually sold and served to the public at all times
and hours during which beer is sold or served for consumption on the premises,
and that the principal business of such place will be the selling and serving
of meals rather than the selling and serving of beer; and
      (9)   Anything else which may be required by the Council.
(Prior Code, § 5-7-7) (Ord. 162, passed 7-1-1958)
§ 112.62 REGULATIONS.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any person to sell or serve beer to any
habitual drunkard or to any intoxicated person.
   (B)   The advertising of beer by any sign, placard, or notice on the outside
of any building within the corporate limits of the city is hereby prohibited.
   (C)   No beer parlor shall sell or serve beer to any woman unless separate
sanitary restrooms are provided for women on the premises.
   (D)   No licensee shall conduct or permit to be conducted, played, or
carried on any game of faro, monte, roulette, lansquenet, rouge et noir, rondo,
Indian stick game, poker, or any game played with cards, dice, or any other
device for money, checks, credit, or any other representative of value upon any
licensed premises.
   (E)   It shall be unlawful for any licensee to sell or serve beer except
upon the licensed premises.
   (F)   No licensee of any place, as defined in §
112.56, licensed for the sale of beer for consumption on the premises, or any
person in charge thereof, or on duty while employed by the licensee therein,
shall permit, suffer, or allow any person under the age of 21 years to enter,
remain in, or loiter in any such place; provided, that this division (F) shall
not apply to bona fide restaurants, as defined in §
112.56.
   (G)   No person shall sell, serve, or dispense beer to any person under the
age of 21 years.
   (H)   No licensee of any place, as defined in §
112.56, licensed to sell beer, or any employee thereof while on duty, shall
bring any intoxicating beverage other than beer on the licensed premises, or
knowingly suffer or permit any intoxicating beverage other than beer to be
brought or consumed on the licensed premises.
   (I)   Whenever any beer parlor is open for business, the interior of the
same shall be kept brightly lighted to the extent that each and every portion
of the interior thereof is clearly visible to any person entering the same.
(Prior Code, § 5-7-8) (Ord. 162, passed 7-1-1958; Ord. 282, passed 12-17-1990)
Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 112.63 LICENSE TRANSFER.
   (A)   No license transferred by operation of law or otherwise shall
authorize the transferee, including any executor, administrator, or trustee in
bankruptcy of the estate of the licensee, to sell beer thereunder until the
transferee shall have filed under oath with the Clerk an application therefor
containing the same information required of an applicant for a license, and
until the Clerk, with the approval and under the direction of the Council, has
authorized the transfer.
   (B)   If the transferee possesses all the qualifications and none of the
disqualifications for a license as herein provided, the Council shall authorize
the transfer. The transferee shall accompany each such application for transfer
with and shall pay the sum of $10 as a license transfer fee.
(Prior Code, § 5-7-9) (Ord. 162, passed 7-1-1958)
§ 112.64 HOURS.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any person in any place licensed to sell
beer, wine, and liquor under this subchapter or where beer, wine, and liquor is
sold or dispensed to be consumed on the premises to sell, serve, or permit
beer, wine, or liquor to be consumed on the premises between the hours of 2:00
a.m. and 6:00 a.m.
   (B)   It shall be unlawful for any person in any place licensed under this
subchapter to sell beer, wine, and liquor to be consumed on the premises to
play or permit to be played any radio, phonograph, television, jukebox, or
other musical instrument between the aforementioned hours.
(Prior Code, § 5-7-10) (Ord. 2004-07, passed 9-27-2004) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 112.65 PROPERTY RIGHT.
   There shall be no vested or property right in any license, or transfer
thereof, issued under this subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 5-7-11) (Ord. 162, passed 7-1-1958)
§ 112.66 REVOCATION; REFUSAL TO ISSUE.
   (A)   The Council may revoke or suspend, for a period not exceeding six
months, any license issued under this subchapter, if, upon a hearing thereon
after five days’ notice to the licensee served personally or by mail upon the
licensee or left with an adult person employed or apparently employed in the
licensed premises, such Council finds that the licensee, or his or her agent,
employee, servant, or other person acting in his or her behalf, has violated
any of the provisions of this subchapter, or has on the licensed premises
violated any of the laws of the state pertaining to the sale of intoxicating
beverages or intoxicating liquor or prohibiting gambling, or has made any false
statement in the application for such license or transfer thereof, or did not
have, or has not retained, the qualifications of a licensee, or had, or has
acquired, a disqualification of a licensee.
   (B)   The Council may refuse to issue a license to sell beer, or revoke any
license therefor already issued, to any person who employs any person whose
license to sell beer has been revoked by the city or the state, or who enters
into a partnership with any such person, or who undertakes with any such person
whose license has been revoked to sell beer as a joint venture, or who leases
the place of business from which such license has been revoked from the person
whose license has been revoked, or who becomes the successor in interest of any
such person with reference to any such place of business.
   (C)   The Council may, on its own motion, institute proceedings for the
revocation or suspension of any license issued under this subchapter, or may
take such action whenever a complaint, in writing and under oath, has been
filed with said Council by any person setting forth facts showing grounds for
revocation or suspension of any such license.
   (D)   Whenever any person shall make complaint, in writing and under oath,
to the Council setting forth facts showing that any license issued under this
chapter is subject to suspension or revocation, the Council shall fix a time
and place for the hearing of the complaint and shall order the licensee to
appear at a time and place specified in the order for hearing. A true and
correct copy of the order, together with a true and correct copy of the
complaint, shall be served personally, by mail upon the licensee or left with
an adult person employed or apparently employed in the licensed premises, at
least five days prior to the hearing. No further pleadings shall be necessary.
If, upon such hearing, the Council finds that cause exists therefor, it may
suspend or revoke the license of the licensee.
(Prior Code, § 5-7-12) (Ord. 162, passed 7-1-1958)
§ 112.67 LICENSE VALIDATION.
   All beer licenses heretofore issued by the city are hereby validated subject
to the provisions of this subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 5-7-13) (Ord. 162, passed 7-1-1958)
§ 112.68 INSPECTION.
   Any police officer of the city, the county, or the state shall have the
right at any time to make an inspection and examination of any premises
licensed under this subchapter to sell beer as to whether the provisions of
this code and the laws of the state are being complied with, and any person
making application under this subchapter for a license to sell beer shall be
deemed to have consented to such inspection and examination.
(Prior Code, § 5-7-14) (Ord. 162, passed 7-1-1958)
§ 112.69 VIOLATION.
   A violation of any of the provisions of this subchapter by any agent,
employee, servant, or other person in any way acting in behalf of the licensee
shall be presumed to be a violation by the licensee.
(Prior Code, § 5-7-15) (Ord. 162, passed 7-1-1958)
CHAPTER 113: TRANSIENT LODGING
Section
Hotels
   
113.01   Defined

113.03   Maintenance of equipment

Motels
   
113.20   Building permit required

HOTELS
§ 113.01 DEFINED.
   Every building maintained or advertised as a public lodging house or where
more than six rooms are provided for sleeping accommodations shall be known as
a HOTEL.
(Prior Code, § 5-4-1)
§ 113.02 FIRE PROTECTION EQUIPMENT.
   The Fire Chief, or other officer designated by the Council, shall survey
each hotel and specify suitable fire detecting devices or extinguishing
appliances which shall be provided.
(Prior Code, § 5-4-2)
§ 113.03 MAINTENANCE OF EQUIPMENT.
   Fire protective or extinguishing systems or appliances which have been
installed in compliance with any permit or order, or according to any
provisions of this code, shall be maintained in operative condition at all
times and it shall be unlawful for any owner or occupant to reduce the
effectiveness of the protection so required.
(Prior Code, § 5-4-3) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 113.04 INSPECTION.
   It shall be the duty of the Fire Chief and the health officer, or other
officers so designated by the Council, to make periodic and regular inspections
of every hotel and to make regular reports to the governing body of such hotel
or hotels concerning regulations imposed by this code.
(Prior Code, § 5-4-4)
§ 113.05 HOTEL REGISTER.
   A register shall be maintained at every hotel, and each guest shall be
required to register his or her name and home address. The date of arrival and
departure shall be clearly indicated, and the register shall be maintained for
a period of at least one year following registration. The register shall be
open for inspection to any authorized person.
(Prior Code, § 5-4-5) Penalty, see §
10.99
MOTELS
§ 113.20 BUILDING PERMIT REQUIRED.
   Before construction of a motel is started, an application for a permit for
such construction shall be submitted to the Clerk. The Clerk shall present such
application to the Council for its approval. Only after approval of the Council
shall a permit for construction of a motel be issued.
(Prior Code, § 5-3-1) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 113.21 SERVICE STATION RESTRICTIONS.
   Automobile service stations shall be located no closer than 50 feet to any
motel.
(Prior Code, § 5-3-2) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 113.22 PARKING SPACE ON PREMISES.
   Each unit of a hotel or tourist court shall be provided with an assigned
parking space entirely on the premises.
(Prior Code, § 5-3-3) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 113.23 MINIMUM REQUIREMENTS.
   The minimum space for each unit shall be 12 feet by 20 feet and shall
contain one full bath, toilet facilities, dressing compartment, and sleeping
room.
(Prior Code, § 5-3-4) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 113.24 EXISTING STANDARDS.
   The plumbing, heating, and ventilation components shall meet all local fire,
plumbing, and building code requirements.
(Prior Code, § 5-3-5) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 113.25 APPLICATION TO INCLUDE PLAN.
   Each application for a motel or tourist court shall be submitted with a
complete plan, including the plot plan and adjacent buildings, parking
arrangement and driveways, unit sizes, plumbing and heating layout, accessory
uses, materials to be used, front and rear elevations, and architectural
design.
(Prior Code, § 5-3-6) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 113.26 GUESTS REQUIRED TO REGISTER.
   Every operator of a motel shall maintain a register in which each guest
shall register his or her name, home address, and license number of the vehicle
in which he or she is traveling. The date of his or her arrival and departure
shall also be recorded. Such register shall be available to any authorized
person inspecting the motel and shall be preserved for a period of not less
than one year.
(Prior Code, § 5-3-7) Penalty, see §
10.99

POOL, BILLIARD HALLS, AND CARD ROOMS
§ 114.01 LICENSE REQUIRED.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any person to operate, maintain, or conduct a
billiard, pool, or bagatelle or pigeonhole table open to the public without
having first obtained a license therefor as is herein required.
   (B)   All applications for such licenses shall state thereon the intended
location of the place of business and the number of tables to be used therein.
(Prior Code, § 5-5-1) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 114.02 FEES.
   Before a license shall be issued to any person to operate or open a
billiard, pool, or card hall or room, said person shall pay to the Clerk a
license fee of $25 per quarter for one card table and $5 per quarter for each
additional card table; and $5 per quarter for each pool or billiard table. Said
license shall expire on the last day of each quarter. The license issued under
the provisions of this subchapter shall be nontransferable.
(Prior Code, § 5-5-2)
§ 114.03 MINORS.
   Minors under the age of 16 years shall under no circumstances frequent,
loiter, go, or remain in any hall licensed hereunder at any time, and it shall
be unlawful for the proprietor of any hall so licensed to allow or permit any
such minor to frequent, loiter, or remain within the hall in violation of the
provisions of this section.
(Prior Code, § 5-5-3) Penalty, see §
10.99
PARADES
§ 114.15 PERMIT.
   No person shall engage in, participate in, aid, form, or start any parade,
unless a parade permit shall have been obtained from the Chief of Police.
(Prior Code, § 6-8-1) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 114.16 EXCEPTIONS.
   The provisions of this subchapter shall not apply to the following:
   (A)   Funeral processions;
   (B)   Students going to and from school classes or participating in
educational activities, providing such conduct is under the immediate direction
and supervision of the proper school authorities; or
   (C)   A governmental agency acting within the scope of its functions.
(Prior Code, § 6-8-2)
§ 114.17 APPLICATION.
   A person seeking issuance of a parade permit shall file an application with
the Chief of Police on forms provided by such officer. Such application shall
be filed not less than three days nor more than 30 days before the date on
which it is proposed to conduct the parade. The application for said permit
shall set forth the following information:
   (A)   The name, address, and telephone number of the person seeking to
conduct such parade;
   (B)   The name and address of the organization for whom the parade is to be
conducted;
   (C)   The name, address, and telephone number of the person who will be the
parade chairperson and who will be responsible for its conduct;
   (D)   The date when the parade is to be conducted;
   (E)   The route to be traveled, the starting point, and the termination
point;
   (F)   The approximate number of persons who, and animals and vehicles which,
will constitute such parade, the types of animals and description of the
vehicles;
   (G)   The hours when such parade will start and terminate;
   (H)   The location by streets of any assembly areas for such parade; and
   (I)   Any other information which the Chief of Police shall find reasonably
necessary to a fair determination as to whether a permit should issue.
(Prior Code, § 6-8-3)
§ 114.18 FEE.
   There shall be paid at the time of filing the application for a parade
permit a fee of $50. Said fee may be reduced or waived at the discretion of the
Mayor for school or public service organizations.
(Prior Code, § 6-8-4) (Ord. 328, passed 3-10-1997)
§ 114.19 STANDARDS FOR ISSUANCE.
   The Chief of Police shall issue a permit as provided for hereunder when,
from a consideration of the application and from such other information as may
otherwise be obtained, he or she finds that:
   (A)   The conduct of the parade will not substantially interrupt the safe
and orderly movement of other traffic contiguous to its route;
   (B)   The conduct of the parade will not require the diversion of so great a
number of police officers of the city to properly police the line of movement
and the areas contiguous thereto as to prevent normal police protection to the
city;
   (C)   The conduct of such parade will not require the diversion of so great
a number of ambulances as to prevent normal ambulance service to portions of
the city other than that to be occupied by the proposed line of march and areas
contiguous thereto;
   (D)   The concentration of persons, animals, and vehicles at assembly points
of the parade will not unduly interfere with proper fire and police protection
of, or ambulance service to, areas contiguous to such assembly areas;
   (E)   The conduct of such parade will not interfere with the movement of
firefighting equipment en route to a fire;
   (F)   The conduct of the parade is not reasonably likely to cause injury to
persons or property, to provoke disorderly conduct, or create a disturbance;
   (G)   The parade is scheduled to move from its point of origin to its point
of termination expeditiously and without unreasonable delays en route; and
   (H)   The parade is not to be held for the sole purpose of advertising any
product, goods, or event and is not designed to be held purely for private
profit.
(Prior Code, § 6-8-5)
§ 114.20 NOTICE OF REJECTION.
   The Chief of Police shall act upon the application for a parade permit
within three days after the filing thereof. If the Chief of Police disapproves
the application, he or she shall mail to the applicant within three days after
the date upon which the application was filed, a notice of his or her action,
stating the reasons for his or her denial of the permit.
(Prior Code, § 6-8-6)
§ 114.21 DRIVING THROUGH PARADES.
   No driver of any vehicle of any type shall drive between the vehicles or
persons comprising a parade when such vehicles or persons are in motion and are
conspicuously designated as a parade.
(Prior Code, § 6-8-7) Penalty, see §
10.99
   Troy - General Offenses

Section
   
130.01   Aid to an offense

§ 130.01 AID TO AN OFFENSE.
   It shall be unlawful for any person, in any way or manner, to aid, abet,
counsel, advise, or encourage any other person in the commission of any of the
acts mentioned herein or in any manner encourage the commission of such offense
hereby defined.
(Prior Code, § 6-1-2) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 130.02 CRUELTY TO ANIMALS.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to torture or beat cruelly, starve, or
otherwise ill treat any animal in his or her care or charge, whether belonging
to himself or herself or any other person.
(Prior Code, § 6-1-8) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 130.03 FALSE PRETENSES.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to obtain any food, drink, goods, wares,
or merchandise under false pretenses, or to enter any public place and call for
refreshments or other articles and receive and refuse to pay for same, or
depart without paying for or satisfying the person from whom he or she received
the food, goods, wares, and merchandise.
(Prior Code, § 6-1-17) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 130.04 GAMBLING.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to deal, play, or conduct, either as
owner, employee, or lessee, whether or not for hire, any game played with
cards, dice, or any other device for money, checks, credit, or other
representation of value.
(Prior Code, § 6-1-21) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 130.05 GENERAL OFFENSE.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to commit any act or fail to perform any
requirement which is prohibited or required by state law, insofar as such laws
are applicable to municipal government.
(Prior Code, § 6-1-22) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 130.06 HYPNOTISTS PROHIBITED.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to practice hypnotism or for any person
to be a subject for such hypnotist; provided, that this shall not apply to
hypnotism as used in the treatment of patients by an accredited doctor of
medicine or doctor of dentistry, nor shall it prohibit the teaching of
hypnotism in any state accredited educational institution which maintains an
academic standard of the college level.
(Prior Code, § 6-1-25) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 130.07 ASSAULT AND BATTERY.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to commit ASSAULT or BATTERY, which is
hereby defined as any wilful and unlawful use of force or violence upon the
person of another.
(Prior Code, § 6-1-4) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 130.08 SWINDLING.
   It shall be unlawful for any person, who by color, or aid of any trick or
sleight of hand performance, or by fraud or by fraudulent scheme, cards, dice,
or device, to win for himself or herself or for another any money or property,
or a representative of either.
(Prior Code, § 6-1-42) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 130.09 VAGRANCY.
   It shall be unlawful for any person without visible means of support and the
physical ability to work not to seek employment or labor, or to refuse to work
when employment is offered him or her; for any person to seek alms as a
business; for any person to roam about from place to place without any lawful
business; for any idle or dissolute person or associate of known thieves to
wander about the streets at a late and unusual hour of the night, or to lodge
in any other place than is kept for lodging purposes without the permission of
the owner of the property or the person in possession thereof; or for any
person to consort habitually with common prostitutes, habitual drunkards, or
any user of narcotics.
(Prior Code, § 6-1-45) Penalty, see §
10.99
CHAPTER 131: OFFENSES AGAINST PROPERTY
Section
   
131.01   Arson
   
131.02   Barbed wire and electric fences

§ 131.01 ARSON.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to commit ARSON, which is hereby defined
as to maliciously and deliberately set fire to or burn or cause to be burned,
or aid, counsel, or procure the burning of any dwelling or other valuable
property either by himself or herself or with others.
(Prior Code, § 6-1-3) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 131.02 BARBED WIRE AND ELECTRIC FENCES.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any person to erect or maintain any electric
fence or any fence constructed in whole or in part of barbed wire, or to use
barbed wire as a guard to any parking lot or parcel of land.
   (B)   This provision shall not apply to property which had such fencing when
this provision was originally passed, nor to properties having such fencing
when annexed into the city.
   (C)   Permits to erect such fencing may be granted by the City Council upon
a showing that:
      (1)   The applicant has an important purpose in seeking the permit;
      (2)   Issuing the permit will not adversely affect adjoining property or
the residents thereof;
      (3)   If needed by grazing, that the applicant has the appropriate amount
of land to make it suitable for grazing;
      (4)   The fence will be as attractive as possible; and
      (5)   The fence will not create an unsafe condition.
(Prior Code, § 6-1-6) (Ord. 334, passed 9-22-1997) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 131.03 DEPOSITS OF INJURIOUS MATERIAL ON THOROUGHFARES.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to deposit, place, or allow to remain in
or upon any public thoroughfare any material or substance injurious to person
or property.
(Prior Code, § 6-1-9) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 131.04 EXPECTORATING ON SIDEWALKS OR IN PUBLIC BUILDINGS.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to expectorate or spit upon any sidewalk
or upon the floor of any public building or room used for public assemblies.
(Prior Code, § 6-1-16) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 131.05 LUG WHEELS PROHIBITED.
   It shall be unlawful for tractors with wheels injurious to pavement to be
permitted upon the public thoroughfares unless the operator of such vehicle
shall first plank such streets.
(Prior Code, § 6-1-30) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 131.06 MALICIOUS INJURY TO PROPERTY.
   It shall be unlawful for any person wilfully and maliciously to injure,
deface, mutilate, remove, pull down, break, or in any manner interfere with or
molest or secrete or destroy any real or personal property belonging to or
under the control of any person.
(Prior Code, § 6-1-31) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 131.07 PETIT LARCENY.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to commit PETIT LARCENY, which is hereby
defined as a larceny when the property taken is of a value of less than $60.
(Prior Code, § 6-1-36) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 131.08 TRESPASSING.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to take down any fence or to let down
any bars or to open any gate in or on the property of another without the
consent of the owner, occupant, or person in charge thereof.
(Prior Code, § 6-1-43) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 131.09 WATER FLOWING UPON STREETS.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to allow any water to flow into or upon
any public thoroughfare.
(Prior Code, § 6-1-46) Penalty, see §
10.99
CHAPTER 132: OFFENSES AGAINST PUBLIC PEACE
Section
   
132.01   Disorderly conduct

§ 132.01 DISORDERLY CONDUCT.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to engage in any illegal or improper
diversion or to use insulting, indecent, or immoral language, or to be guilty
of any indecent, insulting, or immoral conduct or behavior.
(Prior Code, § 6-1-10) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 132.02 DISTURBING THE PEACE.
   It shall be unlawful for any person, wilfully, maliciously, intentionally,
or unnecessarily, to disturb the peace and quiet of another or of any
neighborhood or family or religious congregation or other assembly by loud or
unusual noises or indecent behavior, or by offensive or unbecoming conduct, or
for any person to threaten, quarrel, fight, or provoke an assault or battery or
curse or swear or utter any obscene or vulgar or indecent language in the
presence of another.
(Prior Code, § 6-1-12) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 132.03 LOUDSPEAKERS OR SOUND TRUCKS.
   It shall be unlawful to play, operate, or use any device known as a sound
truck, loudspeaker, or sound amplifier, radio, or phonograph, with loudspeaker
or sound amplifier or any instrument of any kind or character which emits loud
and raucous noises and is attached to and upon any vehicle unless such person
in charge of such vehicle shall have first applied to and received permission
from the Chief of Police to operate any such vehicle so equipped.
(Prior Code, § 6-1-29) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 132.04 MUFFLERS; UNNECESSARY NOISE.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to operate a motor vehicle, including,
but not limited to, a motorcycle, which shall not at all times be equipped with
a muffler upon the exhaust thereof in good working order and in constant
operation to prevent excessive or unusual noise, and it shall be unlawful for
any person operating any motor vehicle to use a cutout, bypass, or similar
muffler elimination appliance.
(Prior Code, § 6-1-33) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 132.05 PLAYING BALL ON STREETS PROHIBITED.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to play ball or throw any ball to and
fro upon any public thoroughfare in the municipality.
(Prior Code, § 6-1-37) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 132.06 RIOT.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to fail or refuse immediately to
disperse upon an order to do so by a police officer, when two or more persons
are assembled for the purpose of disturbing the peace or for the purpose of
committing any unlawful act.
(Prior Code, § 6-1-40) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 132.07 UNLAWFUL ASSEMBLY.
   It shall be unlawful for two or more persons to assemble together for the
purpose of disturbing the peace or for the purpose of committing an unlawful
act and not to disperse upon the command of an officer so to do.
(Prior Code, § 6-1-44) Penalty, see §
10.99
CHAPTER 133: OFFENSES AGAINST JUSTICE AND ADMINISTRATION

§ 133.01 AID IN ESCAPE.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to aid or assist any person to escape
from lawful confinement or to assist any person to escape from the custody of
any peace officer.
(Prior Code, § 6-1-1) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 133.02 ESCAPES.
   It shall be unlawful for any person convicted of any offense or in lawful
custody to escape or attempt to escape.
(Prior Code, § 6-1-15) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 133.03 FALSE REPRESENTATION.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to represent falsely himself or herself
to be an officer of the municipality or who shall attempt to impersonate any
such officer or who shall, without authority, perform any official act therein
on behalf of an officer.
(Prior Code, § 6-1-18) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 133.04 FRAUDULENTLY AVOIDING PAYMENT OF ADMISSION FEES.
   It shall be unlawful for any person fraudulently to enter, without payment
of the proper admission fee, any theater, ballroom, lecture, concert, or other
place where admission fees are charged; provided, however, that nothing herein
contained shall be deemed to prohibit or restrict the free admission of police
officers engaged in the performance of police duties to any place of public
entertainment or amusement.
(Prior Code, § 6-1-19) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 133.05 FURNISHING WEAPONS AND OTHER ARTICLES TO PRISONERS.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to furnish or attempt to furnish or take
into jail or to deliver or attempt to deliver to any prisoner therein confined,
or in the custody of any officer, any weapon, tool, intoxicating liquors, drug,
or other article without the consent of the officer in charge.
(Prior Code, § 6-1-20) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 133.06 GIVING ASSISTANCE TO POLICE OFFICERS.
   It shall be unlawful for any citizen over the age of 18 years to refuse or
neglect to render assistance to any police officer when called upon for such
assistance or aid in the suppression of riot or other unlawful assemblage or in
the arrest of any person who has committed an offense.
(Prior Code, § 6-1-23) (Ord. 328, passed 3-10-1997) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 133.07 RESISTING AN OFFICER.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to interfere willfully with, resist,
delay, obstruct, molest, or threaten to molest any officer of the municipality
in the exercise of his or her official duties.
(Prior Code, § 6-1-39) Penalty, see §
10.99

§ 134.01 DISTRIBUTION OF OBSCENE LITERATURE.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to exhibit, pass, or deliver to another
any obscene, lewd, or indecent book, pamphlet, picture, card, print, paper,
writing, mold, cast, or figure, or to have same in his or her possession.
(Prior Code, § 6-1-11) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 134.02 HOUSE OF PROSTITUTION.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to keep or assist in the keeping of a
house of ill fame or prostitution, or knowingly to reside therein or knowingly
to rent, lease, or permit any person to occupy any house or room owned, leased,
or controlled by him or her for this purpose.
(Prior Code, § 6-1-24) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 134.03 INDECENT EXPOSURE.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to appear in a state of nudity, or in
any indecent or lewd dress or condition in any public place, or in any such
place to make any indecent exposure of his or her person or private parts
thereof or the private parts of another, or to conduct himself or herself in a
lewd or lascivious manner or to appear in any such place in dress not belonging
to his or her sex.
(Prior Code, § 6-1-26) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 134.04 OBSCENE CONDUCT.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to urinate or stool in any place open to
the public view, or to be guilty of any lewd, lascivious, or obscene conduct,
or to sing any lewd or obscene song, ballad, or other words in any public place
or any other place where other persons are present or indecently to exhibit any
animal.
(Prior Code, § 6-1-35) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 134.05 PROSTITUTION.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to pursue or advertise in any manner his
or her vocation as a prostitute or for any person to advertise the profession
of a prostitute or solicit for a prostitute.
(Prior Code, § 6-1-36) Penalty, see §
10.99
CHAPTER 135: WEAPONS OFFENSES
Section
Air Guns, Firearms
   
135.01   Definitions
   
135.02   Discharge of firearms prohibited
   
135.03   Exceptions; permits
AIR GUNS, FIREARMS
§ 135.01 DEFINITIONS.
   Wherever the term FIREARMS is used in this subchapter, the term shall mean
any instrument used in the propulsion of shot, shell, or bullets or other
harmful objects by the action of gunpowder exploded within it, or by the action
of compressed air, propane, acetylene, or other explosive gas or similar
substance within it, or by the power of springs and including what are commonly
known as air rifles, BB guns, and potato guns.
(Prior Code, § 6-5-1) (Ord. 315, passed 1-20-1996)
§ 135.02 DISCHARGE OF FIREARMS PROHIBITED.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to discharge a firearm within the limits
of the municipality; provided, however, that this shall not apply to:
   (A)   A person discharging a firearm in the lawful defense of person or
persons or property; or
   (B)   A person lawfully discharging a firearm on a sport shooting range as
defined in Idaho Code § 55-2604.
(Prior Code, § 6-5-3) (Ord. 2015-03, passed 6-24-2015) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 135.03 EXCEPTIONS; PERMITS.
   The Council may, at any time, upon receipt of proper application, grant
permits to shooting galleries, gun clubs, and others for shooting in fixed
localities and under specified rules. Such permits shall be in writing attested
by the Clerk conforming to such requirements as the Council shall demand, and
the permit thus issued shall be subject to revocation at any time by action of
the Council.
(Prior Code, § 6-5-4)
CHAPTER 136: DRUG OFFENSES
Section
   
136.01   Beer; procuring or selling to minors
   
136.02   Drunkenness

§ 136.01 BEER; PROCURING OR SELLING TO MINORS.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to procure, sell, or give away any beer
to any person under the age of 21 years, or for any person under the age of 21
years to purchase, attempt to purchase, or otherwise procure, consume, or have
in his or her possession any beer.
(Prior Code, § 6-1-7) (Ord. 282, passed 12-17-1990) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 136.02 DRUNKENNESS.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to be found drunk, intoxicated, or under
the influence of intoxicating liquor upon any public thoroughfare or other
public place.
(Prior Code, § 6-1-13) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 136.03 SALE OF CIGARETTES OR TOBACCO TO MINORS.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to sell or give away, directly or
indirectly, to any person under the age of 18 years, any cigarettes, tobacco,
or any compounds of tobacco used in filling up or making up of a cigarette, or
to give or sell any cigarette papers to minors.
(Prior Code, § 6-1-41) (Ord. 328, passed 3-10-1997) Penalty, see §
10.99
CHAPTER 137: OFFENSES BY MINORS
Section
General Provisions
   
137.01   Encouraging delinquency
Curfew
   
137.15   Prohibited hours for minors on streets
   
137.16   Responsibility of parents and guardians
GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 137.01 ENCOURAGING DELINQUENCY.
   It shall be unlawful for any person, by any act or neglect, to encourage,
aid, or cause a child to come within the purview of the juvenile authorities;
and it shall likewise be unlawful for any person, after notice that a driver’s
license of any child has been suspended or revoked, to permit such child to
operate a motor vehicle during the period that such driver’s license is
suspended.
(Prior Code, § 6-1-14) Penalty, see §
10.99
CURFEW
§ 137.15 PROHIBITED HOURS FOR MINORS ON STREETS.
   It is hereby declared to be a misdemeanor for any boy or girl under 16 years
of age to visit any public place or be on the streets, alleys, or public
grounds of the city between the hours of 10:00 p.m. and 5:00 a.m., unless such
minor be accompanied by a parent or guardian, or have written permission in his
or her possession from such parent or guardian to be abroad at such time;
provided, that any such written permission shall be only for a specific time
and date.
(Prior Code, § 6-6-1) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 137.16 RESPONSIBILITY OF PARENTS AND GUARDIANS.
   Any person having the custody of any MINOR, as defined in §
137.15, permitting, allowing, or abetting said minor to violate the provisions
of §
137.15, shall be deemed guilty of contributing to the delinquency of said
minor. The finding that said minor has violated said section shall be
presumptive proof of the contributing to the delinquency of said minor by said
person having the control of such minor.
(Prior Code, § 6-6-2) Penalty, see §
10.99

GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 150.01 MAILBOXES.
   No person shall install or cause to be installed a mailbox on the State
Highway 8 right-of-way portion of Main Street located within the city limits.
(Prior Code, § 7-11-1) (Ord. 2012-02, passed 6-13-2012) Penalty, see §
150.99
§ 150.02 PUBLIC IMPROVEMENTS STANDARDS.
   The “City Of Troy Standard Construction Specifications For Public
Improvements, 1999,” published by the city, providing standards for
construction of streets, curbs, sidewalks, water and sewer systems, and storm
drainage systems, and providing for repair/replacement of unsafe public
walkways, is hereby adopted. Three copies of these standards shall be on file
with the City Clerk for public use. Future versions of these standards may be
adopted by resolution.
(Prior Code, § 7-8-1) (Ord. 99-1, passed 1-11-1999) Penalty, see §
150.99
SIDEWALKS
§ 150.15 SPECIFICATIONS.
   The material and method of constructing sidewalks shall conform in all
respects to the specifications adopted by the Council. These specifications
shall be on file in the Clerk’s office at all times.
(Prior Code, § 7-1-1) Penalty, see §
150.99
§ 150.16 PROPERTY OWNER MUST CONSTRUCT SIDEWALKS.
   It shall be the duty of every property owner, upon notification by the
Council, to construct or repair sidewalks as such is prescribed in said notice.
(Prior Code, § 7-1-2) Penalty, see §
150.99
§ 150.17 FAILURE TO COMPLY.
   If such property owner shall fail, after notification, to construct or
repair any sidewalk, the Council may order same constructed or repaired. The
costs of said work shall be assessed against the property owner for which said
sidewalk was constructed or repaired, and said cost shall become a lien upon
the property.
(Prior Code, § 7-1-3)
SNOW REMOVAL
§ 150.30 DUTY OF OWNER OR TENANT.
   It shall be the duty of the owner or tenant of any premises abutting or
adjoining any public sidewalk to remove all snow and/or ice from such sidewalk.
(Prior Code, § 7-2-1) Penalty, see §
150.99
§ 150.31 NOTICE TO BE GIVEN.
   (A)   It shall be the duty of the municipality to give notice to any owner
or tenant of any property to remove snow and/or ice, which notice shall be sent
by registered mail to the last known address of such owner, tenant, or
occupant.
   (B)   The owner or occupant shall have not more than 24 hours from and after
receipt of such notice, within which to remove the snow and/or ice as set forth
in said notice.
(Prior Code, § 7-2-2) Penalty, see §
150.99
§ 150.32 MUNICIPALITY REMOVAL.
   (A)   Upon failure of an owner or tenant to comply with the provisions of
this subchapter, the municipality shall have the right to remove such snow and/
or ice and assess the cost thereof against the premises abutting the sidewalk.
   (B)   Such assessment to be certified to the County Assessor or other proper
county official having charge of the making of the assessment roll and such
charge shall be placed on the assessment roll and collected in the same manner
as other municipal taxes are collected.
(Prior Code, § 7-2-3)
TREES AND SHRUBBERY
§ 150.45 TREES TO BE TRIMMED.
   Any owner or occupant of any real property shall trim all trees on property
owned or occupied by him or her, overhanging any public thoroughfare, so that
the branches thereon will not interfere with pedestrians or public travel.
(Prior Code, § 7-3-1) Penalty, see §
150.99
§ 150.46 HEDGES AND SHRUBBERY.
   Any owner or occupant of any real property shall maintain all hedges and
shrubbery adjacent to public sidewalks so that no part of said hedges and/or
shrubbery shall extend over any part of a public sidewalk in the municipality.
(Prior Code, § 7-3-2) Penalty, see §
150.99
§ 150.47 INJURY TO TREES AND/OR SHRUBBERY.
   It is hereby declared unlawful for any person, not the owner thereof, or
without lawful authority so to do, wilfully to injure, deface, disfigure, or
destroy any tree or shrub, or to injure, destroy, cut, or pick any flower or
plant, located either on private ground or on any public place or thoroughfare.
(Prior Code, § 7-3-3) Penalty, see §
150.99
§ 150.48 TREES OUTSIDE OF PROPERTY LINE.
   The Council is hereby provided full and complete control over all trees
which are outside of the property lines of privately owned real property.
(Prior Code, § 7-3-4)
§ 150.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code of ordinances.
   (B)   Any person installing or causing to be installed a mailbox on the
State Highway 8 portion of Main Street located within the city limits in
violation of §
150.01 shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and shall be punished by a fine
not to exceed $300, or by imprisonment not to exceed six months, or by both
such a fine and imprisonment. The City Council shall set the fine for this
violation by resolution of the Council. Further, the city shall have the
authority to remove any mailbox installed in violation of §
150.01.
(Prior Code, § 7-11-2)
   (C)   Violation of the standards adopted in §
150.02 shall be a misdemeanor, punishable by a fine of up to $300, or by
incarceration in the county jail for a period not to exceed 30 days, or by both
such fine and imprisonment.
(Prior Code, § 7-8-2)
(Ord. 99-1, passed 1-11-1999; Ord. 2012-02, passed 6-13-2012)
