§ 155.262 NONCONFORMING USES.
   It is the intent of these regulations to control, mitigate, or terminate
uses that do not conform to the regulations specified by this chapter for the
district in which such use is located.
(Prior Code, § 9-9-3) (Ord. 2001-04, passed 8-27-2001)
§ 155.263 RESTRICTION ON ENLARGEMENT AND MAINTENANCE.
   The lawful use of a building or of land which exists at the time of adoption
hereof, although such use does not conform to the regulations specified for the
district in which the use is located, may be continued; provided, that no such
use shall be enlarged or increased nor be extended to occupy a greater area
than that occupied by such use at the time of adoption hereof. Ordinary
maintenance and repair may be made to any nonconforming building, providing
that no structural alterations are made, and providing that the cost of such
work shall not exceed 25% of the assessed valuation of such building in any
one-year period.
(Prior Code, § 9-9-4) (Ord. 2001-04, passed 8-27-2001) Penalty, see §
155.999
§ 155.264 TERMINATION OF NONCONFORMITY.
   If the nonconforming use of land, or a building or operation within a
building, ceases for a continuous period of one year or more, such use or
operation shall be considered abandoned, and the subsequent use of such land,
or building or operation within it, shall be resumed only in accordance with
the regulations specified by this chapter for the district in which such land,
or building or operation is located, subject to the provisions of Idaho Code §
67-6538.
(Prior Code, § 9-9-5) (Ord. 2001-04, passed 8-27-2001) Penalty, see §
155.999
§ 155.265 DAMAGE TO NONCONFORMING BUILDING.
   A nonconforming building damaged or destroyed by fire, flood, or other
disaster to an extent of more than 50% of the appraised value, may be restored
only if made to conform with all the regulations of the district in which it is
located.
(Prior Code, § 9-9-6) (Ord. 2001-04, passed 8-27-2001) Penalty, see §
155.999
§ 155.266 CHANGE IN USE.
   The Planning and Zoning Commission may permit any nonconforming use to be
changed to any specified use; provided, that the Commission determines at a
public hearing, notice of which has been sent to all property owners in the
neighborhood, that the proposed use is not detrimental or objectionable to the
neighborhood.
(Prior Code, § 9-9-7) (Ord. 2001-04, passed 8-27-2001)
§ 155.267 DISTRICT CHANGES.
   Whenever the boundaries of a district shall be changed so as to transfer an
area from one district to another district of a different classification, the
foregoing provisions of this subchapter shall also apply to any nonconforming
uses existing therein.
(Prior Code, § 9-9-8) (Ord. 2001-04, passed 8-27-2001)
DEVELOPMENT AGREEMENTS AND ZONING ENFORCEMENT
§ 155.280 CERTIFICATE OF OCCUPANCY.
   A certificate of occupancy shall be required before any building or use is
occupied. A certificate of occupancy indicates that an onsite inspection has
shown that the building or use complies with this chapter, including any
conditions imposed upon its approval. Occupancy of a building or use without a
certificate of occupancy shall be a violation of this chapter. The issuance of
a certificate of occupancy shall not be construed as approval of any violation
of this chapter that may have been undiscovered during the inspection.
(Prior Code, § 9-10-1) (Ord. 2001-04, passed 8-27-2001) Penalty, see §
155.999
§ 155.281 TEMPORARY CERTIFICATE OF OCCUPANCY.
   A temporary certificate of occupancy may be issued to permit temporary use
of a building in cases where weather prevents the prompt completion of such
required improvements such as landscaping. No temporary certificate of
occupancy shall be issued for more than 90 days.
(Prior Code, § 9-10-2) (Ord. 2001-04, passed 8-27-2001)
§ 155.282 DEVELOPMENT AGREEMENTS.
   (A)   Authority. The city, pursuant to Idaho Code § 67-6509 and §§
155.035 through
155.055, may require, as a condition of rezoning of land, that an owner or
developer make a written development agreement or commitment concerning use or
development of the subject parcel. The development agreement may limit,
restrict, or condition uses on the property being rezoned.
   (B)   Requirements. Prior to requiring or permitting a development agreement
as a condition of rezoning, the city shall determine the following.
      (1)   The development agreement will foster the policies and objectives
of the comprehensive plan.
      (2)   The development agreement will assist the enhancement and stability
of the parcel’s development and use.
      (3)   The development agreement will help to stabilize and enhance the
surrounding properties, developments, and uses.
   (C)   Form of agreements. Development agreements shall be in the form of
legal agreements appropriate for recording. Development agreements must be
approved by the City Council, and shall contain specific provisions for
modification, enforcement, and termination.
   (D)   Recording required. Development agreement commitments shall be
recorded in the office of the County Recorder. Unless modified or terminated by
the city, a commitment is binding on the owner of the parcel, each subsequent
owner, or other person acquiring an interest in the parcel. A commitment which
is binding on the owner of the parcel is unrecorded; however, an unrecorded
commitment is binding on a subsequent owner or other person acquiring an
interest only if that subsequent owner or other person has actual notice on the
commitment.
   (E)   Modification of agreements. Development agreement commitments may be
modified only by permission of the city after complying with the notice and
hearing provisions of Idaho Code § 67-6509 and §§
155.046 and
155.050.
   (F)   Termination of agreement. The zoning decision upon which the use is
based may be reversed upon failure of the requirements of the commitment after
a reasonable time, as determined by the City Council, upon failure of the
owner, each subsequent owner or other persons acquiring an interest in the
parcel to comply with the conditions in the commitment. After complying with
the notice and hearing provisions of Idaho Code § 67-6509 and §§
155.046 and
155.050, the agreement may be terminated by the city. Violation of a written
commitment by the owner, a subsequent owner, his or her agent or lessee shall
be deemed written consent to rezone due to failure of the conditions imposed by
the commitment in accordance with the provisions in this section.
   (G)   Violation. Violation of any condition or commitment in the agreement
shall be a violation of this chapter and subject to civil or penal action.
(Prior Code, § 9-10-3) (Ord. 2001-04, passed 8-27-2001) Penalty, see §
154.999
§ 155.283 FAILURE TO OBTAIN PERMIT.
   Whenever the Administrator becomes aware of an activity for which a permit
is required by this chapter, but for which a permit has not been approved, he
or she shall notify the occupant (and owner if they are not the same) of the
site to immediately cease all unpermitted activity. Notice shall be given by
posting on the site and first class mail. If activity does not cease, the
Administrator shall ask the City Attorney to take prompt action, as authorized
by Idaho Code § 67-6527, to end the unpermitted activity, and if a permit is
not subsequently issued, to require restoration of the site to its original
condition. Required restoration shall include restoration of vegetative cover
where sites have been graded in violation of this chapter.
(Prior Code, § 9-10-4) (Ord. 2001-04, passed 8-27-2001) Penalty, see §
154.999
§ 155.284 ENFORCEMENT ACTION.
   The process for enforcement of this chapter shall be as follows.
   (A)   Notice. The Administrator shall notify the occupant (and owner if they
are not the same) of the violation by first class mail and/or posting on the
site. The notice shall describe the violation, cite the sections of this
chapter being violated, and order the occupant to attain compliance within 30
days or less where public health, safety, or welfare may be endangered.
   (B)   Action by violator. Any person who receives a notice of violation may
request inspection by the Administrator to show that compliance has been
attained within the 30 days allowed or do as follows:
      (1)   File a written request with the Administrator for an extension of
time to attain compliance, with such extensions being limited to a maximum of
60 days and culminated by an inspection to show that compliance has been
attained; or
      (2)   File an appeal of the Administrator’s notice, following the appeals
procedure of §
155.049.
   (C)   Failure to comply. The Administrator shall notify any occupant or
owner who fails to attain compliance within the specified time, or to show on
appeal that a violation has not occurred. The City Council may consider legal
action on the violation at a specified date, time, and place. This notice shall
be posted on the site and sent by first class mail at least 15 days before that
hearing. The description of the violation from the original notice shall be
repeated and the penalties that may be imposed for violations of this chapter
will be cited again.
   (D)   Council action. The City Council may consider action on the violation.
The occupant or owner shall be permitted to present evidence that a violation
has not occurred. If the City Council finds that a violation has occurred, it
may do as follows:
      (1)   Specify a time within which compliance shall be attained or the
matter automatically pursued by the City Attorney;
      (2)   Direct the City Attorney to immediately initiate civil and/or
criminal actions to bring the building or use into compliance; and/or
      (3)   File a notice of no compliance with the County Recorder.
(Prior Code, § 9-10-5) (Ord. 2001-04, passed 8-27-2001)
VARIANCES
§ 155.295 PURPOSES.
   (A)   The Planning and Zoning Commission is empowered to grant variances in
order to prevent or to lessen such practical difficulties and unnecessary
physical hardships inconsistent with the objectives of zoning as would result
from a literal interpretation and enforcement of certain of the regulations
prescribed by this chapter.
   (B)   (1)   A variance shall not be considered a right or special privilege,
but may be granted to an applicant only upon a showing of undue hardship
because of:
         (a)   Special characteristics applicable to the site which deprives it
of privileges commonly enjoyed by other properties in the same zone or
vicinity; and
         (b)   The variance is not in conflict with the public interest.
      (2)   Hardships must result from special site characteristics relating to
the size, shape, or dimensions of a site or the location of existing structures
thereon, from geographic, topographic, or other physical conditions, or from
population densities, street locations, or traffic conditions.
   (C)   Variances are not intended to allow something that others do not have
a permitted right to do. The purpose of a variance is to provide fair treatment
and to see that individuals are not penalized because of site characteristics
beyond their control.
(Prior Code, § 9-11-1) (Ord. 2001-04, passed 8-27-2001)
§ 155.296 ACTION.
   (A)   Variances permitted; findings required. The Planning and Zoning
Commission may grant a variance with respect to fences and walls, site, area,
width, frontage, depth, coverage, front yard, rear yard, side yards, outdoor
living area, height of structures, distances between structures, or landscaped
areas, as the variance was applied for or in modified form if, on the basis of
application, investigation, and evidence submitted, the Commission makes the
following findings.
      (1)   Literal interpretation and enforcement of the regulation would
result in practical difficulty or unnecessary physical hardship inconsistent
with the objectives of this chapter.
      (2)   There are extraordinary site characteristics applicable to the
property involved or to the intended use of the property which do not apply
generally to other properties classified in the same zoning district.
      (3)   Literal interpretation and enforcement of the regulation would
deprive the applicant of privileges enjoyed by the owners of other properties
classified in the same zoning district.
      (4)   The granting of the variance will not constitute a grant of special
privilege inconsistent with the limitations on other properties classified in
the same zoning district.
      (5)   The granting of the variance will not be detrimental to the public
health, safety, or welfare or materially injurious to properties or
improvements in the vicinity.
   (B)   Parking variances; findings required. The Planning and Zoning
Commission may grant a variance with respect to off-street parking facilities
or off-street loading facilities if, on the basis of the application,
investigation, and the evidence submitted, the Commission makes the following
additional findings.
      (1)   Neither present nor anticipated future traffic volumes generated by
the use of the site in the vicinity reasonably require literal interpretation
and enforcement of the regulation.
      (2)   The granting of the variance will not result in the parking or
loading of vehicles on public streets in such a manner as to interfere with the
free flow of traffic.
      (3)   The granting of the variance will not create a safety hazard or any
other condition inconsistent with the objectives of this chapter.
   (C)   Waivers of front yards, fences, walls, hedges. The Planning and Zoning
Commission may grant variances for the waiver of required front yards, fences,
walls, or hedges, based on a substitute plan, which provides equal safety or
esthetics qualities by other means. The substitute plan must:
      (1)   Provide adequate vision clearance for vehicles, both those passing
on the street and those leaving the development site;
      (2)   Include landscaping;
      (3)   Provide a front yard of at least six feet along at least half the
frontage; and
      (4)   Not be detrimental to the public health, safety, or welfare, or be
materially injurious to properties or improvements in the vicinity.
(Prior Code, § 9-11-2) (Ord. 2001-04, passed 8-27-2001)
§ 155.297 DURATION OF APPROVAL.
   The use or construction permitted under the terms of any variance shall be
commenced within a six-month period. If such use or construction has not
commenced within such time period, the variance shall no longer be valid. Prior
to the expiration of the six-month period, the Planning and Zoning Commission
may, upon request of the applicant, extend approval for up to an additional six
months from the original date of approval.
(Prior Code, § 9-11-3) (Ord. 2001-04, passed 8-27-2001)
§ 155.298 APPLICATION FOR VARIANCE.
   (A)   Filing; form. Application for a variance shall be filed with the
Planning and Zoning Commission on a form prescribed by the city, which shall
include any information the Commission deems necessary.
   (B)   Scale drawing. The application shall be accompanied by an accurate
scale drawing of the site and any adjacent property affected, showing all
existing and proposed locations of streets, property lines, uses, structures,
driveways, pedestrian walks, off-street parking and off-street loading
facilities, and landscaped areas.
   (C)   Nonrefundable fee. The application shall be accompanied by the
appropriate fee, which is established by Council resolution and is
nonrefundable.
(Prior Code, § 9-11-4) (Ord. 2001-04, passed 8-27-2001)
§ 155.299 NOTICE REQUIREMENTS.
   A notice of public hearing shall be given not less than 15 calendar days nor
more than 30 calendar days prior to the date of the public hearing by mailing
notices to the adjacent property owners. The notice shall contain the address
or location of property for which the application is taken as well as a brief
description of the nature of the application.
(Prior Code, § 9-11-5) (Ord. 2001-04, passed 8-27-2001)
§ 155.300 APPEALS; FEES.
   Notice of appeal from the Planning and Zoning Commission decision shall be
given to the City Clerk within 15 days of the decision. The notice shall be
accompanied by the appropriate fee, which is established by City Council
resolution and nonrefundable. All appeals shall follow the procedures set forth
in §
155.049.
(Prior Code, § 9-11-6) (Ord. 2001-04, passed 8-27-2001)
§ 155.301 ACTION ON APPEALS BY CITY COUNCIL.
   The City Council, at the next duly held meeting, shall set a date and time
for a public hearing on the appeal and notify those concerned. The Planning and
Zoning Commission shall submit a written decision setting forth reasons for
their action. The Council, after said public hearing, shall render its decision
within 15 calendar days after the filing of such appeal. The Council may by
resolution affirm, reverse, or modify any decision, determination, or
requirements, but before granting any item which was denied by the Planning and
Zoning Commission, or before changing any of the conditions imposed by the
conditions in the use permit, the Council shall make a written decision setting
forth reasons for the action taken. All appeals shall follow the procedures set
forth in §
155.049.
(Prior Code, § 9-11-7) (Ord. 2001-04, passed 8-27-2001)
CONDITIONAL USE PERMITS (CUP)
§ 155.315 INTENT.
   (A)   Certain types of uses require special consideration prior to their
being permitted in a particular district. The reason for special consideration
involves, among other things, the size of the area required for the full
development of such uses, the nature of the traffic problems incidental to
operation of the use, the effect such uses have on any adjoining land uses, and
on the growth and development of the community as a whole.
   (B)   All uses permitted conditionally are declared to possess such unique
and special characteristics as to make impractical their being included as
outright uses in any of the various districts deemed within this chapter. The
authority for the location and operation thereof shall be subject to review and
the issuance of a CUP. The purpose of review shall be to determine that the
characteristics of any such use shall not be unreasonable or incompatible with
the type of uses permitted in surrounding areas, and for stipulating such
conditions as may be reasonable so that the basic purposes of this subchapter
shall be served. Nothing construed herein shall be deemed to require the
Planning and Zoning Commission to grant a CUP.
(Prior Code, § 9-12-1) (Ord. 2001-04, passed 8-27-2001)
§ 155.316 USE PERMIT PREREQUISITE TO BUILDING PERMIT.
   No building permit shall be issued when a CUP is required by the terms of
this chapter, unless a permit has been granted by the Planning and Zoning
Commission and then only in accordance with the terms and conditions of the
CUP. Conditional use permits may be temporary or permanent for any use or
purpose for which such permits are required or permitted by provisions of this
chapter.
(Prior Code, § 9-12-2) (Ord. 2001-04, passed 8-27-2001)
§ 155.317 APPLICATION FOR PERMIT; FEE.
   Application for a CUP shall be made to the Planning and Zoning Commission by
the owner of the affected property, or his or her authorized agent, on a form
prescribed by the city. The application shall be accompanied by such
information as may be required by the city to enable the pertinent criteria to
be applied to the proposal, together with a filing fee. Fees are established by
City Council resolution and are nonrefundable.
(Prior Code, § 9-12-3) (Ord. 2001-04, passed 8-27-2001)
§ 155.318 GENERAL USE PERMIT CRITERIA.
   A CUP may be granted only if the proposal conforms to all the following
general use permit criteria, as well as to all other applicable use permit
criteria.
   (A)   Compatibility. The location, size, design, and operating
characteristics of the proposed development will be compatible with and will
not adversely affect the livability or appropriate development of abutting
properties and the surrounding neighborhood, with consideration to be given to:
      (1)   Harmony in scale, bulk, coverage, and density;
      (2)   The availability of public facilities and utilities;
      (3)   The harmful effect, if any, upon desirable neighborhood character;
      (4)   The generation of traffic and the capacity of surrounding streets;
and
      (5)   Any other relevant impact of the development.
   (B)   Location, design, site planning. The location, design, and site
planning of the proposed development will provide a convenient and functional
living, working, shopping, or civic environment, and will be as attractive as
the nature of the use and its location and setting warrants.
   (C)   Enhancement of area. The proposed development will enhance the
successful operation of the surrounding area in its basic community functions,
or will provide an essential service to the community or region. The use must
be consistent with applicable elements of the comprehensive plan.
(Prior Code, § 9-12-4) (Ord. 2001-04, passed 8-27-2001)
§ 155.319 INVESTIGATIONS.
   The Planning and Zoning Commission shall cause to be made an investigation
of facts necessary to provide information to ensure a decision consistent with
the intent and criteria of this section.
(Prior Code, § 9-12-5) (Ord. 2001-04, passed 8-27-2001)
§ 155.320 PUBLIC HEARINGS.
   (A)   Requirements. Public hearing and legal notification procedures
required by this section shall follow the procedures outlined in §§
155.046 and
155.050. The Planning and Zoning Commission shall also determine whether the
proposal conforms to the general use permit criteria and to other applicable
use permit criteria and may grant or deny the application for the proposed CUP
or require such changes or impose such reasonable conditions of approval as are
in its judgment necessary to ensure conformity to said criteria. The
determination of the Commission shall become final 15 calendar days after the
date of decision unless appealed to the City Council in accordance with the
provisions of this section and §
155.049.
   (B)   Mobile home parks.
      (1)   Whenever application for a mobile home park is considered, there
shall be two public hearings. The first public hearing shall be limited to
consideration of permit criteria relative to land use. Ten calendar days prior
to the hearing, a concept plan shall be submitted to the Planning and Zoning
Commission. The plan shall be drawn at a scale of not less than one inch equals
100 feet and show the following:
         (a)   Existing conditions of the proposed site in terms of land use,
zoning, and circulation systems;
         (b)   Proposed location and number of mobile home spaces; and
         (c)   Proposed locations of accessways.
      (2)   Following the first public hearing, if land use approval is given,
the developer may proceed with preparation of the preliminary site plan of the
park which is to be prepared in accordance with the city subdivision ordinance.
      (3)   Following receipt of the preliminary site plan, within 30 days, it
shall be reviewed by the Planning and Zoning Commission to determine if it is
consistent with the purpose and intent of the city subdivision ordinance.
      (4)   Upon approval or conditional approval of the preliminary site plan,
the developer may proceed with preparation of the final site plan.
      (5)   Following receipt of the final site plan, a second public hearing
shall be scheduled before the Planning and Zoning Commission for the purpose of
review of the final site plan. Action by the Commission shall be to approve,
disapprove, or approve with conditions.
      (6)   Individual approval at one of the two required public hearings does
not constitute final approval.
      (7)   Final approval for mobile home park CUPs shall require approval at
both public hearings, following the sequences of §
155.345(A).
      (8)   The CUP shall be issued with all conditions listed thereon,
following the second required public hearing at which approval has been given.
(Prior Code, § 9-12-6) (Ord. 2001-04, passed 8-27-2001)
§ 155.321 ACTION BY PLANNING AND ZONING COMMISSION.
   The action by the Planning and Zoning Commission upon the application for a
CUP shall be by the majority of the members of the Commission present at the
meeting where the application is considered. If a CUP is denied, the minutes of
the Commission shall clearly state the reasons for denial. In order to grant a
user permit, the findings of the Commission shall be that the establishment,
maintenance, and operation of such use or building applied for will meet the
requirements of this subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 9-12-7) (Ord. 2001-04, passed 8-27-2001)
§ 155.322 CONDITIONS MAY BE IMPOSED.
   (A)   The Planning and Zoning Commission shall designate conditions with the
CUP as it deems necessary to secure the purpose of this subchapter and may
require the guarantees and evidence that such conditions will be complied with.
   (B)   Such conditions may include:
      (1)   Regulation of uses;
      (2)   Special yards, spaces;
      (3)   Fences and walls;
      (4)   Surfacing of parking areas to city specifications;
      (5)   Street dedications and improvements (or bonds);
      (6)   Regulation or points of vehicular ingress and egress;
      (7)   Regulation of signage;
      (8)   Landscaping and maintenance;
      (9)   Maintenance of the grounds;
      (10)   Provisions for open space and parks;
      (11)   Regulation of noise, vibration, odors, or other similar nuisances;
      (12)   Regulation of time for certain activities;
      (13)   Duration of use; and
      (14)   Such other conditions as will make possible the development of the
city in an orderly and efficient manner in conformity with the intent and
purposes set forth in this subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 9-12-8) (Ord. 2001-04, passed 8-27-2001)
§ 155.323 EFFECTIVE DATE.
   No CUP shall become effective until after an elapsed period of 15 calendar
days from the date of the action of the Planning and Zoning Commission.
(Prior Code, § 9-12-9) (Ord. 2001-04, passed 8-27-2001)
§ 155.324 APPEALS; FEES.
   (A)   Filing. During the 15-day period from the date of the action by the
Planning and Zoning Commission, written appeals from action of the Commission
may be taken to the City Council by the applicant or other interested party.
The use permit shall not become effective until the determination of any appeal
pending against it.
   (B)   Notice; fee; procedure.
      (1)   Notice of appeal shall be given to the Planning and Zoning
Commission. The application shall be accompanied by the appropriate fee, which
is established by City Council resolution and nonrefundable.
      (2)   All appeals shall follow the procedures set forth in §
155.049.
(Prior Code, § 9-12-10) (Ord. 2001-04, passed 8-27-2001)
§ 155.325 ADHERENCE TO APPROVED PLAN.
   A CUP shall be subject to the plans and other conditions upon the basis of
which it was granted. Unless a different termination date is prescribed, the
permit shall terminate six months from the effective date of the granting
unless actual construction or alteration, or actual commencement of the
authorized activities, has commenced. However, such period of time may be
extended by the Planning and Zoning Commission, upon application filed at any
time before said period has expired, but in no event shall the order be
extended for more than 12 months from the date the use permit was first
granted.
(Prior Code, § 9-12-11) (Ord. 2001-04, passed 8-27-2001)
§ 155.326 REVOCATION OF PERMIT.
   In the event of a violation of any of the provisions of zoning regulations,
general permit criteria, or in the event of a failure to comply with any
prescribed condition of approval, the Planning and Zoning Commission may, after
notice and hearing, revoke any CUP. The determination of the Commission shall
become final 15 calendar days after the date of the decision, unless appealed
to the City Council.
(Prior Code, § 9-12-12) (Ord. 2001-04, passed 8-27-2001)
§ 155.327 ACTION ON APPEALS BY CITY COUNCIL.
   The City Council, at the next duly held meeting, shall set a date and time
for a public hearing on the appeal and notify those concerned. The Planning and
Zoning Commission shall submit a report setting forth reasons for their action.
The Council, after said public hearing, shall render its decision within 35
calendar days after the hearing on the appeal. The Council may affirm, reverse,
or modify any decision, determination, or requirements, but before granting any
item which was denied by the Planning and Zoning Commission, and before
changing any of the conditions imposed in the use permit, the Council shall
make a written determination setting forth the reasons for their decision. All
appeals shall follow the procedures set forth in §
155.049.
(Prior Code, § 9-12-13) (Ord. 2001-04, passed 8-27-2001)
OFF-STREET PARKING REQUIREMENTS
§ 155.340 GENERAL REQUIREMENTS.
   (A)   When the intensity of use of any building, structure, or premises is
increased through the addition of dwelling units, gross floor seating capacity,
or other units of measurement specified, parking or loading facilities as
required herein shall be provided for such increase in intensity of use.
   (B)   Parking and loading facilities shall be provided whenever the existing
use of a building or structure changes to a new use.
   (C)   Access to parking spaces as required herein for commercial and
industrial uses shall not be less than 12 feet and not more than 40 feet wide
at the curb line.
   (D)   No lawfully existing building shall be deemed to be a nonconforming
building solely because of the lack of any such required spaces; provided, that
space being used for off-street parking or loading in connection with any such
building at the time of the effective date hereof, or amendments thereto, shall
not be further reduced in area or capacity.
   (E)   When the required number of parking spaces is calculated, fractional
numbers equal to or greater than one-third shall be adjusted to the next higher
whole number of spaces.
   (F)   Parking space requirements for a use not specifically mentioned shall
be the same as for a use specified which has similar traffic generating
characteristics.
   (G)   Except as required for dwellings and motels, off-street parking
facilities for several buildings, structures, or uses, or for mixed uses, may
be provided collectively. The total number of spaces so located together shall
not be less than the sum of the separate requirements for each of the buildings
or uses.
   (H)   Parking spaces and access driveways shall be made of a hard surface,
if off-street parking areas have more than four spaces.
   (I)   Lighting used to illuminate off-street parking areas shall be directed
away from residential properties, and such parking areas shall be effectively
screened on any side adjoining property in a residential zone by a wall, or
fence, or hedge to a height of six feet, except for the front yard setback area
of the adjoining residential property, in which case the height shall be three
feet.
   (J)   Required parking spaces for dwellings shall be upon the same premises
as the dwelling, and no parking space shall be located in any required front or
side yard.
(Prior Code, § 9-13-1) (Ord. 2001-04, passed 8-27-2001) Penalty, see §
155.999
§ 155.341 PARKING AREA DESIGN.
   (A)   All public or private parking areas or garages, except those required
in conjunction with a single-family or two-family dwelling on a single lot,
shall be designed, laid out, and constructed in accordance with the provisions
of this section and the minimum standards as set forth in figure 1, “minimum
parking lot requirements.”
   (B)   In any district, driveways or accessways providing ingress and egress
to or from private or public parking areas or garages shall be permitted
together with any appropriate traffic control devices required.
   (C)   In any residential district, public or private parking areas and/or
spaces shall not be permitted in any required yard, except as provided herein.
   (D)   Required parking spaces shall be permitted on driveways in the
required front yard in conjunction with any single-family or two-family
dwelling on a single lot, provided parking is for no more than two vehicles.
   (E)   Public or private parking areas, spaces or garages in any residential
district are permitted in any interior yard that abuts an alley, provided said
parking areas, structures, or spaces shall comply with the parking diagram in
figure 1.
   (F)   In any commercial or industrial district, public or private parking
areas or parking spaces are permitted in any required or interior yard, except
when lot lines of said districts are common with property zoned residentially,
in which case the parking areas shall be not less than ten feet from the lot
line, unless a permanent sight obscuring fence is constructed and maintained
along that portion of the parking abutting the residentially zoned property.
   (G)   (1)   Areas of three or more parking spaces, except in conjunction
with single-family or two- family dwellings on a single lot, shall be served by
a service drive so that no backyard movement or other maneuvering of a vehicle
within a street, other than an alley, will be required.
      (2)   Service drives shall be designed and constructed to facilitate the
flow of traffic, provide maximum safety to pedestrians and vehicular traffic on
the site, but in no case shall two-way and one-way driveways be less than 20
feet wide and 12 feet wide respectively.
   (H)   Public parking areas provided in excess of the requirements of this
section or as a permitted use shall be designed and laid out in conformance
with figure 1.
(Prior Code, § 9-13-2) (Ord. 2001-04, passed 8-27-2001)

§ 155.343 LOADING SPACES.
   (A)   Each off-street loading space shall measure not less than 35 feet by
12 feet and shall have an unobstructed height of 15 feet and shall be made
permanently available for parking and shall be surfaced, improved, and
maintained.
   (B)   Required loading spaces shall be in conformance with the following:
      (1)   Department stores, freight terminals, hospitals, sanitariums,
industrial or manufacturing establishments, retail or wholesale stores or
storage warehouses, or any similar use which has, or intends to have, 10,000
square feet or more, shall provide the following truck loading or unloading
spaces:

§ 155.344 MAINTENANCE.
   Maintenance of all areas provided for off-street parking and loading shall
include removal and replacement of dead and dying trees, grass and shrubs,
removal of trash, weeds, and other debris. MAINTENANCE shall also include
repair of parking and loading surfaces, traffic control devices, signs, light
standards, fences, walls, curbs, and railing. All areas shall provide for
proper drainage of surface water to prevent drainage onto adjacent properties,
roadways, and walkways. Any lights used to illuminate such areas shall be so
arranged as to reflect the light away from the adjoining residential
properties.
(Prior Code, § 9-13-5) (Ord. 2001-04, passed 8-27-2001) Penalty, see §
155.999
§ 155.345 ACCESSIBLE PARKING SPACES.
   (A)   Standards. Accessible spaces shall be provided for disabled people in
accordance with the appendix of the current city adopted edition of the Uniform
Building Code (UBC). Parking and loading accessibility regulations in the UBC
and this section do not supersede the American Disabilities Act (ADA)
regulations in 28 C.F.R. part 36; Appendix A, 4.1.2. (5a, b, c, d, e) as
reflected hereafter.
   (B)   Compliance and existing elements. Alterations to existing parking
facilities shall comply with provisions of this section. Alterations shall not
reduce, or have the effect of reducing, accessibility or usability of any
parking facility. Alterations which would reduce accessibility will provide for
alternative means of accessibility compliant with the provisions of this
section. If compliance with this section is technically infeasible, the
alteration shall provide access to the maximum extent technically feasible. If
existing elements, spaces, essential features, or common area related to
parking facilities are altered, each such altered element, space, feature, or
area shall comply with the applicable provisions in division 1 of the appendix
in chapter 11 of the city adopted Uniform Building Code and CABO/ANSI A1178.1.
Variances shall be reviewed according to §
155.296(B), and be in conjunction with the “reasonable accommodation” language
of ADA standards.
   (C)   Required number. 
Total Number of Parking Spaces in Lot Required Minimum Number of Accessible
                                      Spaces
Total Number of Parking Spaces in Lot Required Minimum Number of Accessible
                                      Spaces
1 to 25                               1
26 to 50                              2
51 to 75                              3
76 to 100                             4
101 to 150                            5
151 to 200                            6
201 to 300                            7
301 to 400                            8
401 to 500                            9
501 to 1,000                          10
1,001 and over                        10, plus 1 for each 100 over 1,000
 
   (D)   Exceptions. At facilities providing medical care and other services
for persons with mobility impairments, parking spaces shall be provided as in
division (C) above, with the following exceptions:
      (1)   Outpatient units and facilities: 10% of the total number of parking
spaces provided serving each such outpatient unit facility; and
      (2)   Units and facilities that specialize in treatment or services for
persons with mobility impairments: 20% of the total number of parking spaces
provided serving each such unit or facility.
   (E)   Dimensions.
      (1)   All accessible spaces shall be a minimum of eight feet in width
plus a five-foot wide adjacent access aisle.
      (2)   One in every eight accessible spaces, but not less than one, shall
have an adjacent aisle eight feet in width and shall be designated as “van
accessible.”
      (3)   All accessible spaces shall be a minimum of 20 feet in length.
      (4)   Passenger loading zones shall provide a pedestrian access aisle at
least five feet wide and 20 feet long adjacent and parallel to the vehicle pull
up space. If there are curbs between the access aisle and the vehicle pull up
space, then a curb ramp shall be provided. At least one passenger loading zone
shall be provided if loading zones are being utilized.
   (F)   Design.
      (1)   Access aisles shall not be restricted by planters, curbs, or wheel
stops.
      (2)   Access aisles shall be level with the parking space.
      (3)   Two accessible spaces may utilize the same adjacent access aisle.
      (4)   Accessible parking spaces shall be designated as reserved for the
disabled by a sign showing the symbol of accessibility. Van accessible spaces
shall have an additional sign “van accessible” mounted below the symbol of
accessibility. Such sign shall not be obscured by a vehicle parking in the
space. A painted accessible symbol shall also be placed in all accessible
spaces. All signage and striping of accessible spaces shall conform to
regulations in Appendix A.4.30 of ADA.
   (G)   Location.
      (1)   Access aisles shall be connected to an accessible route to the
accessible entrance of a building. The parking access aisle must either:
         (a)   Blend with the accessible route; or
         (b)   Have a curb ramp. Such ramp opening must be located within the
access aisle boundaries and not within the parking space boundaries. (See
figure A.)
      (2)   Parking spaces for disabled people and accessible passenger loading
zones that serve a particular building shall be the spaces or zones located
closest to the nearest entrance on an accessible route.
   (H)   Restriping. When a multiresidential (four plus units on one site)
development, commercial, or industrial business, or the city, as an entity,
resurfaces or paints a new striping pattern onto a parking lot containing more
than five spaces, it must provide accessible parking spaces, clearance, and
ramps as required by provisions of the appendix for chapter 11 of the Uniform
Building Code, this section, and the ADA standards for accessible design.
Painting over old lines as maintenance work or nonslurry shall not be construed
to be RESTRIPING for purposes of this section.
(Prior Code, § 9-13-6) (Ord. 2001-04, passed 8-27-2001) Penalty, see §
155.999
LANDSCAPING AND FENCES
§ 155.360 INTENT.
   (A)   The purpose of landscaping is to bring relief from heat, noise, and
glare through proper placement of green plants and trees, and to encourage
pleasant and attractive surroundings.
   (B)   Greenbelts, landscape screening, or buffer yards may be required for
the protection of residential properties from adjacent major arterial streets,
waterways, railroad rights-of-way, or other features.
   (C)   Any new subdivision or special development must meet the requirements
for landscaping as set forth in the subdivision ordinance.
(Prior Code, § 9-14-1) (Ord. 2001-04, passed 8-27-2001)
§ 155.361 BUFFER YARD REQUIREMENTS.
   (A)   Buffer yards shall be provided in accordance with provisions in this
section whenever any use, development, or modification to use or development is
being reviewed under this chapter.
   (B)   Table 1, “Required Buffer Yards Between Zoning Districts,” is hereby
adopted as part of this section. The letter designation in Table 1 refers to
the buffer yard standards established in §
155.363(B).
   (C)   Buffer yard requirements shall vary depending on the intensity of both
the zoning district of the proposed use and its neighbors. Three different
standards, A, B, and C, are hereby established to accommodate the range of
buffer yard needs. Buffer yards shall conform to the minimum standards provided
in §
155.363(B).
   (D)   All required buffer yards shall be located on the perimeter of a lot
or parcel upon which the development occurs and shall extend from lot line to
lot line, or in an alternative location if the applicant demonstrates that it
will provide an equivalent or superior buffering effect between uses. Buffer
yards shall not be located on any portion of a public or private street,
dedicated right-of-way, or vision clearance triangle.
   (E)   The minimum size of plants at the time of planting shall be as
follows:
      (1)   Canopy trees: one and one-half inch caliper;
      (2)   Understory trees: four feet in height;
      (3)   Shrubs:
         (a)   Deciduous: 15 inches in height; and
         (b)   Evergreen: 12 inches in height.
      (4)   Evergreen trees: three feet in height.
   (F)   Existing trees and other vegetation may be used in combination for
buffering if they are healthy and will satisfy the requirements of this
section.
   (G)   Whenever buffering is required, a buffer yard plan, which may be
incorporated into any other site plan required to be submitted under this
chapter, shall be prepared showing the approximate location, height, size, and
type of all plantings, fences, berms, and irrigation systems.
   (H)   All buffering required by this section shall be installed prior to
occupancy or commencement of use. A building permit shall be issued only upon
completion of all improvements required herein, assuring that a reasonable time
of completion is attained. REASONABLE TIME OF COMPLETION under this section
shall be defined as no longer than 12 months after issuance of the building
permit.
   (I)   The maintenance of buffer yards required by this section is a
continuing obligation of the property owner. The use of property for which a
building permit is issued shall be conditional upon the continued satisfaction
of the requirements of this section.
(Prior Code, § 9-14-2) (Ord. 2001-04, passed 8-27-2001) Penalty, see §
155.999
§ 155.362 FENCES.
   A fence, hedge, wall, column, pier, post, or any similar structure, or any
combination of such structures, may be permitted in the required yards of the
various districts, subject to the following conditions and requirements. It is
intended that these conditions and requirements shall provide privacy and
protection, and screening and accenting of shrubs and landscaping, without
unduly interfering with the view from neighboring properties or jeopardizing
the safety of pedestrians or vehicles.
   (A)   It shall be the responsibility of the property owner to locate all
property lines.
   (B)   No fence, hedge, or wall may extend beyond or across a property line
unless in joint agreement with the abutting property owner.
   (C)   No fence, hedge, or wall shall be placed nearer than 12 inches to any
public sidewalk.
   (D)   No barbed wire or other sharp, pointed, or electrically charged fence
shall be permitted, except as follows.
      (1)   Temporary fences on construction sites may be as high as required
to protect the property during the period of construction and may have barbed
wire where it is not less than eight feet above ground.
      (2)   In the Industrial/Agricultural District, an electrically charged
fence or battery operated fence may be permitted if used to contain livestock.
      (3)   The Industrial District may have barbed wire not less than eight
feet above ground.
   (E)   Fences, walls, or compact hedges shall not exceed seven feet in
height. Height, including walls or other structures, shall be measured as
follows.
      (1)   In required yards abutting a street, it shall be the total
effective height measured from the finished grade on the side nearest the
street.
      (2)   In other required yards, it shall be the total effective height
above the finished grade measured on the side nearest the abutting property.
      (3)   On property lines, the height may be measured from the finished
grade of either side when the abutting property owners are in joint agreement.
      (4)   Parks and schools where play activities take place may have fences
and back slope exceeding the maximum height in this section.
   (F)   On corner lots, no fences, hedge, structure, wall, or landscaping
display shall interfere with the unobstructed view over 36 inches above the
nearest street in a restricted triangular area formed by the three points
established by:
      (1)   The intersection of the property lines at the corner; and
      (2)   By measuring 30 feet back from the intersection on each property
line, except that rail type fences not exceeding 42 inches in height, with more
than two four-inch rails, mounted on a minimum number of four-inch posts, may
be permitted in the restricted triangular area.
(Prior Code, § 9-14-3) (Ord. 2001-04, passed 8-27-2001) Penalty, see §
155.999

§ 155.999 PENALTY.
   Violations of this chapter shall be a misdemeanor, and shall be punishable
by a fine in any amount not exceeding $300 or by imprisonment for a period of
not longer than 30 days, or by a fine and imprisonment. Each day in which a
violation continues, it shall be considered a separate offense. The city may
also use any available civil remedy to enforce this chapter.
